Permissible Animals and Age for Udhiyah
Ruling on permissible animals and age requirements for udhiyah with proof from Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four types of animals permissible for udhiyah and identify the minimum age requirements, explaining the Hanafi position on the jadh' from sheep with its proof.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is only valid from camels, cattle, sheep, or goats, with the thani from all, and the jadh' from sheep at 6 months is valid.

This lesson establishes the types of animals that may be sacrificed (udhiyah) and the required ages. The Hanafi school limits udhiyah to four domestic species and defines specific age thresholds. A special ruling applies to the jadh' from sheep, which is permitted at six months based on prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible animal types
List the four categories: camels, cattle, sheep, and goats (ghanam). These are the only animals allowed for udhiyah.
Wild animals are excluded.
2
State the general age requirement (thani)
The thani (second-year animal) is required for all types: sheep/goats 1 year, cattle 2 years, camels 5 years.
This is the standard age for musinnah.
3
Learn the exception: jadh' from sheep
The jadh' (6-month-old sheep) is also permissible, based on the hadith: 'Do not slaughter except a musinnah unless it is difficult, then slaughter a jadh' from sheep.'
This is a concession with conditions.
4
Apply the condition of size for jadh'
The jadh' must be large enough to resemble a thani when mixed, as stated by the Hanafi jurists.
This ensures it is substantial enough for sacrifice.
5
Note the definition of jadh' and thani
Jadh' from sheep: 6 months (Hanafi) or 7 months (al-Za'farani). Thani: sheep/goats 1 year, cattle 2 years, camels 5 years.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'i requires 1 year for jadh'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأضحية من الإبل والبقر والغنم، وجاز الثني من الكل، والجذع من الضأن، لقوله علي: "لا تذبحوا إلا مسنة إلا أن يعسر عليكم، فتذبحوا جذعة من الضأن"، رواه البخاري ومسلم وأحمد وجماعة أخر، وقال عليه: "نعمت الأضحية الجذع من الضأن"، رواه أحمد، وقال عليه: "يجوز الجذع من الضأن أضحية"، رواه أحمد وابن ماجه. قالوا هذا إذا كان الجذع عظيما بحيث لو خلط بالثنيات ليشتبه على الناظرين. والجذع من الضأن ما تمت له ستة أشهر عند الفقهاء، وذكر الزعفراني أنه ابن سبعة أشهر. والثني من الضأن والمعز ابن سنة، ومن البقر ابن سنتين، ومن الإبل ابن خمس سنين. [تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٣/٨]
And the sacrifice is from camels, cattle, and sheep/goats. And the thani (two-year-old) from all is permissible, and the jadh' (one-year-old) from sheep, due to his saying: 'Do not slaughter except a musinnah (older animal) unless it is difficult for you, then slaughter a jadh' from sheep.' Narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, and others. And he said: 'An excellent sacrifice is the jadh' from sheep,' narrated by Ahmad. And he said: 'The jadh' from sheep is permissible as a sacrifice,' narrated by Ahmad and Ibn Majah. They said: This is when the jadh' is large such that if mixed with thanis, it would be similar to the viewers. The jadh' from sheep is one that has completed six months according to the jurists, and al-Za'farani mentioned it is seven months. The thani from sheep and goats is one year old, from cattle is two years old, and from camels is five years old. [Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 353/8]
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the types of animals permissible for udhiyah and their required ages. It begins by stating that udhiyah is confined to four types: camels, cattle (including buffalo as noted earlier), and sheep/goats (ghanam). The matn then states that the thani (second-year animal) from each type is permissible, and the jadh' from sheep is also permissible. The proof is a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ: 'Do not slaughter except a musinnah (older animal) unless it is difficult, then slaughter a jadh' from sheep.' This is narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. The hadith indicates that the ideal is a musinnah (thani), but a jadh' is allowed when needed. Furthermore, the Prophet ﷺ praised the jadh' as excellent and explicitly permitted it. The commentary clarifies that the jadh' must be large enough to resemble a thani. The definitions: jadh' of sheep is 6 months (or 7 according to al-Za'farani); thani of sheep/goats is 1 year; thani of cattle is 2 years; thani of camels is 5 years. These ages are standard in the Hanafi school. The passage concludes with a reference to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. This lesson combines the rulings on animal type and age, emphasising that the sacrifice is not valid from wild animals (like wild ox) and that only domestic cattle, camels, sheep, and goats are permitted.

Key Terms
الجذع (al-jadh'): A sheep that has completed six or seven months.
الثني (al-thani): A second-year animal: sheep/goats one year, cattle two years, camels five years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Six months (jadh').
C) Two years.
D) Five years.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the jadh' from sheep at six months for udhiyah, provided it is large enough, based on prophetic hadith.

Joint Sacrifice: Death, Non-Muslim Partners, and Shares by Istihsan
Three rulings on joint sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on joint sacrifice when a partner dies, when a partner is non-Muslim, and when two partners share an animal, and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
In joint sacrifice, istihsan permits what qiyas forbids: a deceased partner’s share, a half share, and the requirement of pure intention.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents three scenarios of joint sacrifice (udhiyah). Each ruling hinges on the concept of qurbah (religious devotion) and the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference). The text demonstrates how the school prioritizes the underlying intent of worship over strict analogical reasoning when necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three cases: (1) death of one of seven partners, (2) a partner who is Christian or apostate, or who intends only meat, (3) two partners sharing a cow or camel.
Each scenario has a distinct ruling based on conditions like intention and share size.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For scenario (1): valid by istihsan if heirs give permission. Scenario (2): invalid for all. Scenario (3): by qiyas invalid, but the more correct view (by istihsan) is valid.
Note the role of istihsan in scenarios (1) and (3).
3
Analyze the qiyas argument for two partners
Qiyas: A cow suffices for seven, so each partner's share must be at least one-seventh. Half is less, so invalid. Identify the original case (asl) and the new case (far').
The illa (effective cause) is the insufficiency of the share amount.
4
Understand the istihsan counter-argument
Istihsan: The half share is not independent; it becomes a valid qurbah by dependence on the other partner's share. The entire animal is one act of worship.
This overrides qiyas because the purpose of qurbah is achieved.
5
Identify the key condition that invalidates
In scenario (2), the condition of qurbah (intention of worship) is absent. A non-Muslim cannot intend qurbah, and intention of meat destroys the worship nature. This nullifies the entire joint sacrifice.
Intention is paramount in acts of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات أحد السبعة وهم كبار، وقالت الورثة: اذبحوها عنه وعنكم صح استحسانا. وإن كان شريك الستة نصرانيا أو مرتدا، أو نوى اللحم، لم يجز عن واحد منهم. ولو اشترك اثنان في بقرة أو بعير لا يجوز في الأضحية؛ لأنه يكون لواحد منهم ثلاثة أسهم ونصف، والنصف لا يجوز في الأضحية، والأصح أنه يجوز؛ لأن النصف يصير قربة بطريق التبع لغيره. [تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٣/٨]
And if one of the seven people dies, and they are adults, and the heirs say: 'Sacrifice it on his behalf and on your behalf,' it is valid by istihsan. And if the partner of the six is a Christian or an apostate, or intends the meat, it is not valid for any of them. And if two people share in a cow or a camel, it is not valid for sacrifice, because one of them would have three and a half shares, and half is not valid in sacrifice; but the more correct view is that it is valid, because the half becomes a sacrifice by way of dependence on the other. [Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 353/8]
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage addresses joint sacrifice (ishtirak) in udhiyah. The first scenario: seven people purchase a badana (camel) together for sacrifice. If one of them dies before slaughter, the heirs can give permission to sacrifice on behalf of the deceased and the living partners; this is valid by istihsan because the sacrifice is a form of charity and can benefit the deceased. The proof is that the Prophet ﷺ sacrificed on behalf of his entire Ummah, so sacrificing on behalf of a deceased person is valid. The second scenario: if one of the seven partners is a Christian or an apostate, or if any partner intends to eat the meat (i.e., no intention of qurbah), then the sacrifice is invalid for all. This is because the act of sacrifice requires religious intent (qurbah), which a non-Muslim or someone with worldly intention lacks. The third scenario: two partners share a single cow or camel (which normally suffices for seven). According to qiyas, it should be invalid because one partner's share is 3.5 out of 7 (half the animal), and half an animal is insufficient for udhiyah. However, by istihsan the more correct view holds it valid because the share of one partner becomes a qurbah by dependence on the other's share (the half becomes part of a whole intended for sacrifice). This is a clear example of istihsan overriding qiyas.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas for a stronger reason, such as a text, necessity, or custom.
القربة (al-qurbah): An act of drawing near to Allah; the intention of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If seven people buy a camel for udhiyah and one of them dies before slaughter, what is the ruling if the heirs give permission?
A) The sacrifice is invalid because the deceased cannot own.
B) It is valid by istihsan if the heirs agree.
C) Only the living six can sacrifice.
D) The animal must be sold and the proceeds given in charity.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, joint sacrifice remains valid even when a partner dies or when shares are uneven, provided the intention of worship is maintained and istihsan permits departure from strict analogy.

Eating the Meat of Udhiyah: General Permission and Vow Exception
Rulings on consumption and distribution of udhiyah meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating udhiyah meat, identify the prophetic proof, and distinguish the exception for vowed (nadhr) sacrifices.

Core Idea
Eating from udhiyah is permitted, but if vowed, it becomes charity and the sacrificer may not eat.

This lesson examines the ruling on consumption and distribution of udhiyah meat. The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's hadith, permits eating, storing, and feeding others. However, a key distinction arises when the sacrifice is obligatory by vow: the meat must be entirely given in charity.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
The Hanafi school permits the sacrificer (mudhi) to eat from his udhiyah meat, to feed others (whether rich or poor), and to store it. This is based on the prophetic permission.
This applies to sunnah udhiyah and wajib udhiyah that is not by vow.
2
Examine the prophetic proof
The hadith 'كلوا وتزودوا وادخروا' (Eat, take provisions, and store) narrated by Muslim and al-Nasa'i abrogates the earlier prohibition of keeping meat beyond three days. The imperative indicates permissibility.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted for action.
3
Identify the exception for vowed sacrifices
When the udhiyah is wajib by nadhr (vow), the meat must be given entirely in charity. The sacrificer cannot eat any of it, nor feed rich people. If he eats, he must pay the value.
This is because a vowed udhiyah becomes like sadaqah; the giver cannot benefit from it.
4
Apply the ruling to different scenarios
Distinguish: (a) Sunnah udhiyah: permissible to eat and store. (b) Wajib udhiyah (non-vow): same as sunnah. (c) Wajib by nadhr: must give all in charity; no eating.
For (c), if the sacrificer eats, he must compensate the value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويأكل من لحم الأضحية، ويؤكل غنيا أو فقيرا ويدخر. لما روي أنه عليه النهى عن أكل لحوم الضحايا بعد ثلاثة ثم قال: "كلوا وتزودوا وادخروا"، رواه مسلم والنسائي. وإذا جاز أن يأكل منه وهو غني فأولى أن يجوز له إطعام غيره وإن كان غنيا، كذا في "العيني". [تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٧٠/٢] وقال في "الفتح": وهذا في الأضحية الواجبة والسنة سواء إذا لم تكن واجبة بالنذر، وإن وجبت بالنذر، فليس له أن يأكل منها شيئا، ولا أن يطعم غيره من الأغنياء، سواء كان الناذر غنيا أو فقيرا؛ لأن سبيلها التصدق، وليس للمتصدق أن يأكل من صدقته ولا أن يطعم الأغنياء، ولو أكل فعليه قيمة ما أكل. [زيلعي عناية]
And he eats from the meat of the sacrifice, and it is eaten, whether rich or poor, and stored. Due to what was narrated that the Prophet ﷺ forbade eating the meat of sacrifices after three days, then said: 'Eat, take provisions, and store.' Narrated by Muslim and al-Nasa'i. If it is permissible for him to eat from it while he is rich, then it is more appropriate that it is permissible for him to feed others, even if they are rich. Thus in al-'Ayni. [Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 370/2] And he said in al-Fath: This applies equally to obligatory (wajib) and sunnah sacrifice, as long as it is not obligatory by vow (nadhr). But if it is obligatory by vow, then he may not eat any of it, nor may he feed other rich people, whether the one who made the vow is rich or poor; because its purpose is charity (sadaqah), and the giver of charity may not eat from his charity nor feed the rich. If he does eat, then he must pay the value of what he ate. [Zayla'i, 'Inayah]
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of the sacrificer (mudhi) eating the meat of his udhiyah. The hadith initially forbade keeping meat beyond three days, then the Prophet ﷺ allowed eating, taking provisions, and storing. Therefore, the sacrificer and others (whether rich or poor) may eat the meat. The commentary from al-'Ayni states that if the sacrificer, being rich, may eat, then he may also feed other rich people. Finally, al-Fath distinguishes between a sunnah udhiyah and a wajib udhiyah by vow (nadhr). In the latter case, the meat must be given entirely in charity; the sacrificer cannot eat any of it, nor feed rich people, because it is like sadaqah. If he does eat, he must pay its value. This distinction is important: a regular udhiyah (sunnah or wajib) allows consumption, but a vowed udhiyah is exclusively for charity.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow; making a particular act of worship obligatory upon oneself by a pledge.
التصدق (al-tasadduq): Giving in charity; the required disposition of meat from a vowed udhiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, he can eat even if he is rich.
B) No, he cannot eat any of it; it must be given in charity.
C) He can eat only if he is poor.
D) He can eat only after three days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits eating from udhiyah meat, but prohibits it when the sacrifice is obligatory by vow.

Prohibition of Gold and Silver Vessels and Permissibility of Other Metals
Ruling on using gold/silver vessels, permissibility of other metals, and conditions for silver-plated items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using gold and silver vessels, explain the permissibility of other metals, and apply the condition for silver-plated items.

Core Idea
Gold and silver vessels are haram; other metals are halal; silver-plated items are halal if the silver is avoided.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the general prohibition of gold and silver vessels for both men and women, based on a clear hadith. It then clarifies that vessels made from other metals such as lead, glass, and brass are permissible, contrary to the Shafi'i view. Finally, it addresses silver-plated items, detailing an intra-Hanafi difference and the condition that one must avoid contact with the silver.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that drinking from gold or silver vessels is haram for men and women. Determine that the act is using gold/silver vessels, and the ruling is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Hudhayfah (Bukhari and Muslim) is cited as proof. Identify that the hadith explicitly forbids drinking from gold and silver vessels.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'la tashrabu' indicates prohibition (nahy yufid al-tahrim). Explain how this yields the ruling of haram.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Two levels: (a) Inter-madhhab: Shafi'i dislikes other metals; Hanafi permits. (b) Intra-madhhab: On silver-plated items, Abu Hanifa permits with condition; Abu Yusuf dislikes; Muhammad is inconsistent.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's permissibility of silver-plated items with the condition of avoiding the silver.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من إناء ذهب وفضة للرجل والمرأة، لا من رصاص وزجاج وبلور وعقيق، وحل راجع للجميع الشرب من إناء مفضض ، والركوب على سرج مفضض، والجلوس على كرسي مفضض ويتقي موضع الفضة، ويقبل قول الكافر ولو مجوسيا
من إناء ذهب إلخ لما روي عن حذيفة الله أنه قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: "لا تلبسوا الحرير ولا الديباج، ولا تشربوا في آنية الذهب والفضة، ولا تأكلوا في صحافها، فإنها لهم في الدنيا، ولكم في الآخرة"، رواه البخاري ومسلم فإذا ثبت ذلك في الأكل والشرب، فكذا في التطيب وغيره؛ لأنه مثله في الاستعمال، ويستوي فيه الرجال والنساء؛ لإطلاق الحديث، وكذا الأكل بملعقة الذهب والفضة والاكتحال بميلهما، والمرآة والمجمرة وما أشبه ذلك، وفي "الذخيرة": الادهان المحرم أن يأخذ آنية الذهب والفضة، ويصب الدهن على الرأس منها، أما إذا أدخل يده فيها، وأخذ الدهن ثم صبه على الرأس من اليد لا يكره [رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۳/۲] وفي ما نقله من "الذخيرة" كلام طويل مذكور في "التكملة" و"الفتح" أورد عليه بعضهم، وأجاب عنه آخرون، من شاء فليرجع إليهما. لا من رصاص إلخ: أي لا يكره الأكل والشرب والادهان والتطيب من رصاص وزجاج وبلور وعقيق، وقال الشافعي: يكره جميع ذلك؛ لوقوع التفاخر بها، قلنا: لا نسلم ولئن سلمنا، فهي ليست في معنى الذهب والفضة، فلم تلحق بهما، ويجوز استعمال الأواني من الصفر؛ لما ثبت في البخاري وغيره أنه عليها توضأ من تور من صفر". [رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۳/۲] :وبلور بكسر الباء وفتح اللام كسنور، وفتح الباء وضم اللام، لغتان. ويتقي إلخ: أي حل الشرب والركوب والجلوس المذكور بشرط أن يجتنب موضع الفضة بالفم، وقيل: بالفم واليد في الأخذ وفي الشرب، وفي السرج والكرسي موضع الجلوس، ومثل ما ذكر من الإناء المفضض وغيره الإناء المضبب بالذهب والفضة، والكرسي المضبب بهما، وكذا لو جعل ذلك في نصل السيف والسكين أو في قبضتهما، ولم يضع يده في موضعهما، وكذا لو جعل في حلق المرآة، أو جعل المصحف مذهبا أو مفضضا، وكذا المفضض من اللجام والركاب والثفر.
وكذا الثوب إذا كان فيه كتابة بذهب أو فضة وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو يوسف: يكره ذلك كله، ومحمد مضطرب وهذا الاختلاف فيما يخلص، وأما التمويه الذي لا يخلص فلا بأس به بالإجماع؛ لأنه مستهلك، فلا عبرة ببقائه لونا، واحتج أبو حنيفة بما روي عن أنس الله " أن قدح النبي انكسر، فاتخذ مكان الشعب فضة"، رواه البخاري. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۳/۲] قال في "الفتح": والمضبب المشدود بالضباب جمع ضبة، وهي جريدة عريضة كما في "العناية": قال في "الاختيار": وأما اللجام من الفضة، والركاب من لأنه استعمل الفضة بعينها.
سلسلة من الفضة، فحرام؛
From vessels of gold and silver for men and women, not from lead, glass, crystal, and agate; and permissible for all is drinking from a silver-plated vessel, riding on a silver-plated saddle, and sitting on a silver-plated chair, provided one avoids the place of silver. And the statement of a disbeliever, even a Magian, is accepted. 'From vessels of gold, etc.' based on what was narrated from Hudhayfah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Do not wear silk and brocade, and do not drink from vessels of gold and silver, and do not eat from their plates, for they are for them in this world and for you in the Hereafter.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. So when this is established for eating and drinking, it applies similarly to perfuming and other things, because it is analogous in usage. And it is equal for men and women due to the generality of the hadith. Similarly, eating with a gold or silver spoon, applying kohl with a gold or silver applicator, mirrors, incense burners, and the like. In al-Dhakhira: The prohibited oil application is to take a gold or silver vessel and pour oil from it onto the head. As for inserting the hand into it, taking the oil, then pouring it onto the head from the hand, it is not disliked. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/373). And what he transmitted from al-Dhakhira contains lengthy discussion mentioned in al-Takmila and al-Fath; some criticized it and others responded; whoever wishes may refer to them. 'Not from lead, etc.': i.e., it is not disliked to eat, drink, apply oil, and perfume from lead, glass, crystal, and agate. Al-Shafi'i said: All that is disliked due to pride in them. We say: we do not accept, and even if we accept, they are not analogous to gold and silver, so they are not included with them. And it is permissible to use brass vessels, as established in Bukhari and elsewhere that he performed ablution from a brass vessel. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/373). 'Balur': with kasra of ba and fatha of lam like 'sanawwar', and with fatha of ba and damma of lam, two languages. 'Wattaqi, etc.': i.e., the drinking, riding, and sitting mentioned are permissible on condition that one avoids the place of silver with the mouth, and it is said: with the mouth and hand when taking and drinking, and for the saddle and chair, the place of sitting. And similar to what is mentioned of the silver-plated vessel and others is the vessel plated with gold and silver, and the chair plated with them, and similarly if that is placed on the blade of a sword or knife or on their handles, and one does not place one's hand on their spots, and similarly if placed on the ring of a mirror, or if the Quran is made gilded or silvered, and similarly the silvered parts of the bridle, stirrup, and crupper. And similarly the garment if it has writing in gold or silver. All this is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: All that is disliked. Muhammad is inconsistent. And this difference concerns that which is substantive. As for plating that does not leave a residue, there is no harm by consensus, because it is consumed, so its remaining color is of no consequence. Abu Hanifa argued based on what was narrated from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet's drinking cup broke, so he replaced the broken part with silver, narrated by Bukhari. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/373). He said in al-Fath: 'Al-mudabbat' is tightened with 'dibab', plural of 'dabba', which is a wide plate, as in al-Inayah. He said in al-Ikhtiyar: As for a bridle made of silver and a stirrup made of silver, it is haram because silver itself is used. A chain of silver is haram.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on eating and drinking presents the ruling on using vessels made of gold and silver. The matn states that drinking from gold or silver vessels is prohibited (haram) for both men and women. The prohibition is established by the hadith of Hudhayfah narrated in Bukhari and Muslim, which explicitly forbids drinking from gold and silver vessels. The ruling extends to all forms of use, including eating, applying perfume, using spoons, kohl applicators, mirrors, and incense burners. The commentator notes that the prohibition applies to direct use, but if one pours oil from a gold vessel onto the hand and then applies, it is not disliked. Vessels made of other metals (lead, glass, crystal, agate, brass) are permissible, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who dislikes them due to ostentation. The Hanafi response is that these materials are not analogous to gold and silver. The passage then discusses silver-plated items (mufaddad): it is permissible to drink from a silver-plated vessel, ride on a silver-plated saddle, or sit on a silver-plated chair, provided one avoids contact with the silver (e.g., by not putting the mouth on the silver part). This condition applies to other items like plated swords, knives, mirrors, and gilded Qurans. An intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded: Abu Hanifa permits such usage with the condition of avoiding the silver, while Abu Yusuf dislikes it, and Muhammad's position is inconsistent. However, all agree that silver plating that does not leave a substantive residue (tamwih) is permissible by consensus. Abu Hanifa supports his view with the hadith of the Prophet's cup that was repaired with silver. The passage concludes with a mention that a bridle or stirrup made purely of silver is haram, and a chain of silver is likewise haram.

Key Terms
مفضض (mufaddad): An object plated or inlaid with silver, not made entirely of silver.
التمويه (al-tamwih): Plating that does not leave a substantive residue; the silver is consumed and only color remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram because it involves silver.
B) It is permissible only if one avoids placing the mouth on the silver part.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It is permissible unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
Gold and silver vessels are haram; other metals are halal; silver-plated items require avoiding the silver part.

Acceptance of Reports in Transactions vs. Religious Matters
Explains ruling on accepting reports in mu'amalat vs diyanat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mu'amalat and diyanat regarding the acceptance of reports, and apply the Hanafi rule that reports of non-Muslims, slaves, children, and fasiqs are accepted in transactions but not in religious matters.

Core Idea
In transactions, necessity opens the door to any discerning person's report; in religion, only the just are trusted.

Everyday transactions require flexibility: we often rely on reports from people we wouldn't trust for religious testimony. The Hanafi school clarifies this through a fundamental distinction between mu'amalat (dealings between people) and diyanat (matters between the servant and Allah). In this lesson, we explore the ruling, its proof from consensus, and the practical implications, including how to handle a report from a sinful or non-Muslim person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Domains
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between mu'amalat (transactions, e.g., agency, trade) and diyanat (religious matters, e.g., purity of water, halal meat). For each, the condition for accepting a report differs.
Mu'amalat concern rights between people; diyanat concern obligations toward Allah.
2
State the Default Ruling for Each Domain
In mu'amalat, the report of any discerning (mumayyiz) person is accepted, whether Muslim or non-Muslim, free or slave, adult or child, upright or sinful. In diyanat, only the report of a just ('adl) person is accepted; otherwise, the hearer must investigate (taharrī).
The key condition for mu'amalat is mere discernment (tamyiz); for diyanat, it is uprightness ('adalah).
3
Examine the Evidence (Dalil)
The basis is consensus (ijma) that the report of a disbeliever is accepted in transactions, because transactions are frequent, and requiring uprightness would cause hardship (haraj). The same logic extends to all discerning individuals.
Consensus is a strong proof, though its transmission (al-thubut) is zanni; its meaning (al-dalalah) is clear.
4
Understand the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Al-Zayla'i objected that the passage's example (meat from a Jew) seems to involve a religious ruling (halal/haram). The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Ayni reply: the permissibility here is implicit (al-hall al-dhimni) – it arises within the transaction, not as an independent religious report.
The principle: if a non-Muslim reports 'I bought this meat from a Muslim,' his word is accepted because the report is about the transaction, not about the meat's inherent permissibility.
5
Apply the Ruling to Specific Examples
The passage lists: a Magian servant reporting meat purchase, a slave reporting a gift, a child reporting a gift, and a fasiq reporting in transactions. In all these, the report is accepted. For diyanat (e.g., water purity), the hearer must investigate based on strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann).
If a fasiq claims water is impure, you are not bound to accept it; you do taharrī and act on your predominant inference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
ما يتعلق بالأكل والشرب
في الحل والحرمة والمملوك والصبي في الهدية والإذن، والفاسق في المعاملات،
الحاصلين في ضمن المعاملات
في التجارة
كالوكالات ونحوها
في الحل والحرمة إلخ حتى لو كان له أجير مجوسي أو خادم مجوسي فأرسله ليشتري له لحما، فاشترى لحما، وقال: اشتريته من يهودي أو نصراني أو مسلم وسعه أكله، وإن كان غير ذلك لم يسعه أن يأكله. واعلم أن قول الكافر إنما يقبل فيما إذا كان متضمنا لهما، فأما إذا صرح بهما، فلا يقبل؛ لأنهما من الديانات، وقول الكافر لا يقبل في الديانات، فلو قال: يقبل قول الكافر في اشتراء اللحم من يهودي أو نصراني، لكان أولى، كذا في "ملا مسكين"، وقال في "الفتح" عند قول الشارح ملا مسكين حتى لو كان له أجير مجوسي أو خادم مجوسي"، كذا ذكره المصنف في "الكافي".
سهو؛
لأن
ثم قال: وأصله أن خبر الكافر في المعاملات مقبول بالإجماع؛ لصدوره عن عقل ودين مانع من الكذب، ومساس الحاجة إلى قبوله؛ لكثرة المعاملات وكونه من أهل الشهادة أي على مثله فهذا هو القرينة على أن المراد بالحل والحرمة ما يكون في ضمن المعاملات لا مطلقا كما توهمه ،الزيلعي فاعترض على المصنف، وقال: هذا الحل والحرمة من العبادات، ولا يقبل قول الكافر في الديانات وإنما يقبل في المعاملات، والظاهر أن الزيلعي لم يطلع على كلام المصنف في "الكافي"، وإلا لما وسعه الاعتراض عليه. وأجاب العيني عن اعتراض الزيلعي بما حاصله أن هذا ليس بسهو، وهذا المقدار لا يخفى على مثل المصنف، وإنما أراد بالحل الحل الضمني وبالحرمة الحرمة الضمنية؛ لأنه أراد بهذا الكلام، حاصل المسألة التي ذكرها صاحب الهداية بقوله: "من أرسل أجيرا له مجوسيا إلخ" ، قال في "الفتح" بعد ذكر الجواب عن المصنف: ثم رأيت العلامة الوافي قال: لقائل أن يقول: هذا لا يدفع الاعتراض عن ظاهر كلام "الكنز". والمملوك إلخ : يعني يقبل قول المملوك، سواء كان عبدا أو جارية، وقول الصبي في الهدية، بأن قال المملوك: هذه هدية أهداها إليك سيدي، أو قال الصبي: هذه هدية أهداها إليك أبي، وفي "الجامع الصغير": إذا قالت جارية لرجل: بعثني مولاي إليك هدية وسعه أن يأخذها؛ لأنه لا فرق بين ما إذا أخبرت بإهداء المولى غيرها أو نفسها، وإنما يقبل قول هؤلاء فيها؛ لأن الهدايا تبعث عادة على أيدي هؤلاء، وكذا يقبل قولهما في الإذن أي في إذن المولى لعبده، وإذن الولي للصبي؛ لأنه لا يمكن استصحاب الشهود على الإذن عند الضرب في الأرض والمبايعة في السوق، فلو لم يقبل قولهما يؤدي إلى الحرج. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٧٤/٢]
:
في الهدية سواء أخبر بإهداء المولى نفسه أو غيره والفاسق في المعاملات [ سواء كان حرا أو عبدا ذكرا أو انثى مسلما أو كافرا (ملا)] أي وكذا يقبل قول الفاسق في المعاملات كالتوكيل والإذن في التجارة، وكل شيء ليس فيه إلزام، ولا ما يدل على النزاع لأجل الضرورة، والأصل فيه: أن المعاملات يقبل فيها خبر كل مميز حرا كان أو عبدا مسلما كان أو كافرا صغيرا أو كبيرا؛ لأنها كثيرة، واشتراط العدالة فيها يؤدي إلى الحرج، فيشترط فيه التمييز لا غير، ولا دليل مع التسامح يعمل به سوى الخبر، فلو لم يقبل خبره لامتنع باب المعاملات، ووقعوا في حرج عظيم، وبابه مفتوح رمز الحقائق: ٣٧٤/٢]
لا في الديانات كالإخبار بحل الطعام وحرمته وطهارة الماء ونجاسته ] لأنها لا تكثر وقوعا، فلا حرج في اشتراط العدالة فيها، ولا حاجة إلى قبول قول الفاسق؛ لأنه متهم واعلم أن المعاملات ما يكون فيما بين العباد، والديانات ما يكون بين الرب ،والعبد، فالأول مثل الوكالات والمضاربات والإذن في التجارات والثاني كالإخبار بحل الطعام وحرمته وطهارة الماء ونجاسته والشهادة بهلال رمضان وأخبار النبي الله الله حتى لو أخبر فاسق بنجاسته ووقع في قلبه كذبه، جاز التوضؤ، بخلاف قول العدل، كذا في "شرح القدوري" و"الفتح" و"ملا مسكين"، وقال العيني: حتى إذا أخبره عدل أنه نجس يتيمم ولا يتوضأ به، وإذا أخبره فاسق تحرى فيه، وكذا إذا كان مستورا في الصحيح، فإن غلب على ظنه أنه صادق يتيمم ولا يتوضأ به، وإن أراقه ثم تيمم كان أحوط ولو كان أكبر رأيه أنه كاذب يتوضأ ولا يتيمم، لترجح جانب الكذب. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٧٤/٢]
The Book of Disliked Acts. Regarding eating and drinking, concerning permissibility and prohibition, and the slave and the child regarding gifts and permission, and the sinner in transactions, [these matters] occur within transactions... in trade, such as agency agreements and the like. He said: 'Concerning permissibility and prohibition, etc., even if he has a Magian employee or a Magian servant, and he sends him to buy meat, and he buys meat and says, "I bought it from a Jew, a Christian, or a Muslim," it is permissible for him to eat it. If it is otherwise, it is not permissible for him to eat it.' Know that the statement of the disbeliever is only accepted if it is implicit in these two matters. As for when he explicitly mentions them, it is not accepted, because they are matters of religion, and the statement of a disbeliever is not accepted in religious matters. So if one says, 'The statement of the disbeliever is accepted regarding purchasing meat from a Jew or Christian,' then it is more appropriate. Thus in 'Mulla Miskin'. He said in 'al-Fath' concerning the commentator Mulla Miskin's statement: 'Even if he has a Magian employee or a Magian servant'—thus mentioned the author in 'al-Kafi'. [He said: 'This is a mistake? Because...'] Then he said: The origin is that the report of a disbeliever in transactions is accepted by consensus, because it arises from reason and a religion that prevents lying, and due to the pressing need to accept it because transactions are frequent, and because he is among those eligible for testimony regarding similar matters. This is the indication that is meant by 'permissibility and prohibition' as within transactions, not absolutely, as al-Zayla'i imagined. So he objected to the author, saying: 'This permissibility and prohibition pertains to acts of worship, and the statement of a disbeliever is not accepted in religious matters; it is only accepted in transactions.' It appears that al-Zayla'i was not aware of the author's words in 'al-Kafi'; otherwise, he would not have been able to object. Al-Ayni replied to al-Zayla'i's objection, the essence being that this is not a mistake, and such a point is not hidden from someone like the author. Rather, he intended by 'permissibility' the implicit permissibility, and by 'prohibition' the implicit prohibition, because by this statement he meant the outcome of the issue that the author of al-Hidayah mentioned with his words: 'Whoever sends his Magian employee, etc.' He said in 'al-Fath' after mentioning the reply to the author: 'Then I saw al-Allamah al-Wafi say: One may say that this does not rebut the objection to the apparent wording of al-Kanz.' And 'the slave, etc.' means the statement of the slave is accepted, whether male or female slave, and the statement of the child regarding gifts, such as if the slave says, 'This is a gift that my master gave to you,' or the child says, 'This is a gift that my father gave to you.' In 'al-Jami' al-Saghir': If a slave woman says to a man, 'My master sent me to you as a gift,' it is permissible for him to take it, because there is no difference between whether she reports the master's gift of someone else or of herself. The statements of these persons are accepted in this matter because gifts are customarily sent through them. Similarly, their statements are accepted regarding permission, i.e., the master's permission to his slave, and the guardian's permission to the child, because it is not possible to maintain witnesses for permission when traveling in the land and transacting in the market. If their statements were not accepted, it would lead to hardship. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/374] 'Regarding the gift, whether he reports the master's gift of himself or someone else, and the sinner in transactions [whether free or slave, male or female, Muslim or disbeliever (Mulla)]' i.e., similarly, the statement of the sinner is accepted in transactions such as deputyship and permission in trade, and everything that does not involve obligation, nor indicates conflict, due to necessity. The principle is: In transactions, the report of every discerning person is accepted, whether free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever, young or old, because transactions are many, and requiring uprightness in them would lead to hardship. Therefore, only discernment is required, and nothing else. In the face of laxity, there is no proof that is acted upon except the report. If his report were not accepted, the entire field of transactions would be prevented, and they would fall into great hardship, and its door is open. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/374] 'Not in religious matters', such as reporting the permissibility or prohibition of food, or the purity or impurity of water, because these do not occur frequently, so there is no hardship in requiring uprightness in them, and there is no need to accept the statement of a sinner because he is suspect. Know that transactions concern what is between people, and religious matters concern what is between the Lord and the servant. The former includes deputyships, partnerships, and permission in trades; the latter includes reporting the permissibility or prohibition of food, the purity or impurity of water, testifying to the crescent of Ramadan, and reports of the Prophet [etc.]. So if a sinner reports its impurity and in his heart he considers him a liar, it is permissible to perform ablution with it, contrary to the statement of a just person. Thus in 'Sharh al-Quduri', 'al-Fath', and 'Mulla Miskin'. Al-Ayni said: Even if a just person reports that it is impure, he performs tayammum and does not perform ablution with it. If a sinner reports it, he investigates. Similarly, if the reporter is of unknown character (mastur), according to the sound position: if he strongly presumes him to be truthful, he performs tayammum and does not perform ablution with it; if he pours it away and then performs tayammum, it is more precautionary; if his greater opinion is that he is lying, he performs ablution and does not perform tayammum, because the side of falsehood is preponderant. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/374]
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the beginning of Kitab al-Karahiyyah, addresses a core principle of Hanafi fiqh: the distinction between mu'amalat (transactions) and diyanat (religious matters) regarding the acceptance of reports. The author establishes that in transactions, reports from any discerning person—whether Muslim, disbeliever, free, slave, adult, child, or sinner—are accepted due to necessity and the impossibility of always having upright witnesses. The proof is consensus and the need to avoid hardship. The key distinction is between the implicit permissibility/prohibition (al-hall wa al-hurmah al-dhimniyyah) that arises within transactions and the explicit religious rulings. Al-Zayla'i's objection is refuted by noting that the permissibility here is implicit, not absolute. The passage then details the acceptance of a slave's report in gifts, a child's report in gifts, and a sinner's report in transactions, all due to common practice and necessity. The final portion distinguishes diyanat from mu'amalat: for religious matters like water purity, only just ('adl) witnesses are accepted; if a fasiq reports, the hearer must investigate (taharrī). If he is strongly convinced of truthfulness, he may do tayammum; if he strongly leans falsehood, he may use the water. This ruling comes from the later authorities (muta'akhkhirin) and is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
المعاملات (al-muʿāmalāt): Transactions and dealings between people, such as agency, partnership, and trade.
الديانات (al-diyānāt): Religious matters between the servant and the Lord, such as purity, forbidden food, and testimony for Ramadan crescent.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion of lying that invalidates acceptance of a report in religious matters.
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): Uprightness and just character required for acceptance of testimony or report in religious matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a fasiq (sinner) reports that a well's water is najis (impure), what must the hearer do?
A) He must accept it and perform tayammum unconditionally.
B) He must reject it since a fasiq is not trustworthy.
C) He must investigate (taharrī) and act based on his strong presumption.
D) He must not use that water at all.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, reports in transactions (mu'amalat) are accepted from any discerning person out of necessity, while in religious matters (diyanat) only the report of a just person is accepted, with the hearer otherwise investigating based on strong presumption.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on Looking and Touching in Hanafi Fiqh
Comprehensive section on looking at non-mahram, mahram, and between genders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at a non-mahram free woman and apply the exceptions for necessity (judge, marriage, medical).

Core Idea
Looking at a non-mahram woman's face and hands is permissible without desire; all else is forbidden.

In this passage from the Book of Disliked Matters, the author lays out the foundational rulings on looking (nazar) and touching (lams) between genders. The default position is strict: only the face and hands of a free woman are permitted to be seen, and only when free from desire. However, necessity creates exceptions for judges, witnesses, doctors, and those intending marriage. Understanding these rules is essential for daily interactions and for grasping the Hanafi approach to balancing modesty with practical needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: looking at a free non-mahram woman. State the default: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to look at anything except her face and hands (wajh and kaffayn).
The phrase 'la yanzuru' implies prohibition (haram) for other parts.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse 24:31 is cited: '...and not show their adornment except what appears.' Explain that companions Ali and Ibn Abbas interpreted 'what appears' as the face and hands (the places of kohl and ring).
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala due to interpretation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'illa ma zahara' creates an exception; the impermissibility of other parts is derived from the general command to conceal. The necessity of social interaction (muamalat, walking, etc.) supports the exception.
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas due to necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on specifics
Identify the dispute on whether the foot is 'awrah. The text states that the correct view (in al-Hidayah) is that it is not 'awrah, but some say it is for looking and touching. Also note Abu Yusuf's view allowing forearms due to custom.
The mufta bihi is that foot is not 'awrah.
5
Evaluate exceptions and conditions
List exceptions: judge, witness, doctor, circumciser, and one intending marriage may look even with desire if necessary. For those without necessity, looking with desire is absolutely haram. Also note the ruling for women looking at women: recommended to lower gaze if desire arises, unlike men for whom it is obligatory.
Necessity overrides the general prohibition but with minimal exposure.

كتاب الكراهية
فصل في النظر واللمس
لا ينظر إلى غير وجه الحرة وكفيها ولا ينظر من اشتهى إلى وجهها إلا الحاكم
فصل في النظر إلخ لما أنهى الكلام على مسائل اللبس وقدمه؛ لشدة الاحتياج إليه، ذكر بعده مسائل النظر؛ لأنها أكثر وقوعا من مسائل الاستبراء؛ فلذا قدمها، ومسائل النظر أقسام أربعة نظر الرجل إلى المرأة، ونظر المرأة إلى الرجل، ونظر الرجل إلى الرجل، ونظر المرأة إلى المرأة، والقسم الأول منها على أربعة أقسام: نظر الرجل إلى الأجنبية، ونظره إلى زوجته وأمته ونظره إلى ذوات محارمه ونظره إلى أمة الغير، وبين المصنف أحكامها، وبدأ بالقسم الأول من أقسام نظر الرجل إلى المرأة تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٨٣/٨]
لا ينظر إلى غير إلخ أي لا يجوز النظر إلى غير وجه الحرة وكفيها وليس في كلام المصنف التحريض على النظر إلى هذين العضوين كما ادعاه الزيلعي واعلم أن إطلاق قول المصنف: "لا ينظر إلى غير وجه الحرة" إلخ يتناول لما إذا كان الناظر للحرة عبدها، وبه صرح في الدرر" حيث قال لمملوكها أن ينظر إلى وجه سيدته وكفيها لا قدميها وسيذكره المصنف آخر هذا الفصل بقوله: "وعبدها كالأجنـ أجنبي". فتح ا الله المعين) يجوز له أن ينظر إلى وجه الحرة وكفيها سواء كانت شابة أو عجوزا وإنما جاز النظر إليها؛ لقوله تعالى: وَلا يُبْدِينَ زِينَتَهُنَّ إِلَّا مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْهَا﴾ (النور: (۳۱) قال علي وابن عباس : "ما ظهر منها الكحل والخاتم"، والمراد به موضعهما، وهو الوجه والكف كما أريد بالزينة محلها، ولأن في إبدائهما ضرورة؛ لحاجتها إلى المعاملة مع الرجال والإعطاء وغير ذلك من المخالطة كالمشي في الطريق، وكما لا يجوز النظر فكذا الخلوة. قال في "الدر" عن الأشباه الخلوة بالأجنبية حرام إلا لملازمة مديونة هربت ودخلت خربة وفيما إذا كانت عجوزا شوهاء وفيما إذا كان بينهما حائل وفيه عنها الخلوة بالمحرم مباحة إلا الأخت من الرضاعة والصهرة الشابة، وما عدا ما استثنى من الأعضاء لا يجوز له أن ينظر إليه؛ لقوله عليه "من نظر إلى محاسن امرأة عن شهوة صب في القيامة"، ولا يحل له أن يمس وجهها ولا كفيها وإن كان يأمن الشهوة، هذا أي جواز النظر إنما هو إذا لم يكن النظر عن شهوة، فإن كان يعلم أنه إن نظر اشتهى لم يحل النظر إلى شيء منها. (فتح) وكفيها فيه إشارة إلى أن القدم عورة، وفيه خلاف، ففي الهداية": الأصح أنه ليس بعورة، وقيل: الصحيح أنه عورة في حق النظر والمس، وليس بعورة في حق الصلاة والمشي وعن أبي يوسف أنه يباح النظر إلى ذراعيها؛ لأنه يبدو منها عادة. (عيني، فتح) ولا ينظر إلخ أراد أن صاحب الشهوة لا يجوز له أن ينظر إلى وجهها أي وجه الحرة مع جواز النظر إليه عند عدم الشهوة رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۲۸] إلا الحاكم إلخ : [ وكذا مريد نكاحها ولو عن شهوة بنية السنة. (ط) فإنهما ينظران مطلقا للضرورة في إحياء الحقوق، والأصل أنه لا يجوز أن ينظر إلى وجه الأجنبية بشهوة لما روينا؛ إلا للضرورة إذا تيقن بالشهوة أو شك فيها، وفي نظر من ذكرنا مع الشهوة ضرورة =
عينيه
والشاهد، وينظر الطبيب إلى موضع مرضها وينظر الرجل إلى الرجل إلا العورة
إذا أرادا الحكم والشهادة وكذا نظر قابلة وختان فقط
والمرأة للمرأة والرجل كالرجل للرجل، وينظر الرجل إلى فرج أمته وزوجته، ......
أي وتنظر اللام بمعنى إلى
وإلى سائر بدنها التي يحل له وطئها
، فيجوز، وكذا نظر الحاقنة والحاقن، وكذا نظر الخاتن إذا أراد أن يداوي مع الختان، وكذا يجوز النظر للهزال الفاحش؛ لأنه أمارة المرض، ولكن يجب على القاضي والشاهد قصد أداء الشهادة والحكم لا قضاء الشهوة تحرزا عن القبيح بقدر الإمكان، وهذا وقت الأداء، وأما وقت التحمل، فلا يجوز أن ينظر إليها مع الشهوة؛ لأنه يوجد من لا يشتهي، فلا حاجة إليه. (فتح، تكملة، عيني) وينظر الطبيب إلخ: للضرورة، ولكن يستر كل عضو منها سوى موضع المرض، ثم ينظر ويغض بصره عن غير ذلك الموضع ما استطاع، وينبغي أن يعلم امرأة إن أمكن لأن نظر الجنس أخف، وإلا ينظر على الوجه الذي ذكرناه رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۲] إلا العورة: أي لا ينظر الرجل إلى عورة الرجل، وهي ما بين السرة إلى الركبة، والسرة ليست من العورة والركبة منها، وإنما لم ينبه المؤلف هنا لما قدم في "كتاب الصلاة"، وقد بينا الدليل هناك، وحكم العورة في الركبة أخف منه في الفخذ وفي الفخذ أخف منه في السوأة حتى ينكر عليه في كشف الركبة برفق، وفي الفخذ بعنف، وفي السوأة بضرب إن لج. [تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٨٦/٨] والمرأة إلخ: معناه: المرأة في النظر إلى المرأة والرجل كالرجل في النظر إلى الرجل يعني كما ينظر الرجل إلى الرجل، وهو جواز النظر إلى جميع البدن غير العورة، وهذا إذا أمنت الشهوة والفتن وإن كان في قلبها شهوة، أو في أكبر رأيها أنها تشتهي أو شكت في ذلك، يستحب لها أن تغض بصرها، بخلاف الرجل عند الشهوة، يجب عليه أن لا ينظر والفرق أن الشهوة غالبة عليهن وهي كالمتحقق حكما، فإذا اشتهى الرجل كانت الشهوة موجودة من الجانبين، وإذا اشتهت هي لم توجد إلا منها، فكانت من جانب واحد، والموجود من الجانبين أقوى، وما جاز للرجل أن ينظر إليه جاز مسه؛ لأنه ليس بعورة، بخلاف مسه في المرأة، وكل عضو لا يجوز النظر إليه قبل الانفصال لا يجوز بعده ولو بعد الموت كشعر عانته وشعر رأسها وعظم ذراع حرة ميتة وساقها، وقلامة ظفر رجلها دون يدها. (تكملة، فتح، عيني) والرجل: أي تنظر المرأة إلى الرجل أيضا كالرجل إلخ أي كنظر الرجل الرجل فلا تنظر المرأة إلى ما بين سرة المرأة. (ط) وينظر الرجل: وكذلك المرأة والأمة إلى زوجها ومولاها. (ط) إلى فرج أمته إلخ. سواء كان بشهوة أو بغيرها؛ لقوله علي غض بصرك إلا عن زوجتك وأمتك"، والمراد بالأمة التي يحل وطئها وأما إذا كانت لا تحل كالأمة المجوسية أو المشركة أو أخته رضاعا أو أم امرأته وأمثالها فلا يحل النظر إلى فرجها، والأولى أن لا ينظر كل واحد منهما إلى عورة صاحبه؛ لأنه يورث النسيان، وكان ابن عمر لما يقول: الأولى أن ينظر إلى فرج امرأته وقت الوقاع؛ لأنه أبلغ في تحصيل معنى اللذة رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۲] (تكملة)
Book of Disliked Matters. Chapter on Looking and Touching. He does not look at other than the face and palms of a free woman, and one who desires should not look at her face except the judge. ...
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive exposition from the Hanafi school on the rulings of looking (nazar) and touching (lams). It begins by stating the default ruling: it is not permissible to look at any part of a free non-mahram woman except her face and hands. This is derived from the Quranic verse (24:31) where 'what appears' is interpreted as the face and hands by Ali and Ibn Abbas. The ruling is based on necessity for transactions and social interaction. Looking with desire is prohibited entirely, except for judges and those intending marriage due to necessity. The text then discusses exceptions for witnesses, doctors, circumcisers, etc., requiring them to minimize looking. Regarding looking between men and women, the 'awrah of a man is from navel to knee, with varying degrees of strictness for different parts. Women looking at women is analogous to men looking at men, but with a difference: a woman is recommended to lower her gaze if she feels desire, whereas a man is obliged. The passage concludes with rulings on touching and looking at one's wife and slave, allowing looking at private parts for the purpose of intimacy, though it is better to avoid looking at the 'awrah to prevent forgetfulness.

Key Terms
الحرة (al-hurrah): The free woman, as opposed to a slave woman, in the context of looking rulings.
الكفيين (al-kaffayn): The two hands, including palms and back of hands up to the wrist.
القدم (al-qadam): The foot, including the top and sole. Dispute on whether it is 'awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which parts of a free non-mahram woman's body is it permissible to look at without desire?
A) Face and forearms
B) Face and hands
C) Face and feet
D) Only the face

Key Takeaway
The default ruling: only face and hands are permissible to look at, and only without desire; all other parts are 'awrah and prohibited.

The Obligation of Istibra' for a Purchased Slave Woman
Ruling with proof for istibra' of a purchased slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of istibra', identify its proof from the hadith of the captives of Autas, and apply the conditions to determine when it is wajib.

Core Idea
Istibra' is wajib upon the buyer of any slave woman — certainty of empty womb does not remove the obligation.

Istibra' is a waiting period required when a slave woman changes ownership. It protects lineage by ensuring the womb is free of the previous owner's pregnancy. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and a key difference within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the text says about the permissibility of intercourse with a newly purchased slave woman: it is forbidden until istibra' is completed. The ruling is that istibra' is wajib.
The prohibition covers intercourse, touching, and looking with desire.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith from the captives of Autas. The text quotes part of it.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves obligation. The imperative 'لا توطأ' indicates prohibition, and 'حتى يستبرأن' specifies the condition. The driver of obligation is the new ownership.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf allows omitting istibra' when certainty of empty womb exists (e.g., seller is a woman). The majority position (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) requires it absolutely.
The text explicitly rejects Abu Yusuf's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude which position is relied upon for fatwa: the absolute obligation, as it aligns with the zahir of the hadith and is the stronger opinion.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاستبراء وغيره من ملك أمة حرم وطئها ولمسها والنظر إلى فرجها بشهوة حتى تستبرئ، فصل في الاستبراء إلخ: الاستبراء في اللغة: طلب البراءة، وفي الشرع : طلب براءة الرحم من الحمل. (عيني، فتح) أمة: أي استمتاع أمة فيخرج شراء الرجل زوجته. (فتح) حرم وطئها إلخ أي مطلقا سواء تيقن فراغ رحمها من ماء البائع بأن يكون مالكها امرأة أو صبيا، أو تكون الجارية بكرا أو نحوه، أو لم يتيقن، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه إذا تيقن فراغ رحمها من ماء البائع، فليس عليه الاستبراء. ملا) (مسكين حتى تستبرئ إلخ: بأن يتركها إلى أن تحيض حيضة واحدة إن كانت من ذوات الحيض، أو يمضي عليها شهر واحد إن كانت آئسة، أو إلى أن تضع حملها إن كانت حاملا؛ لقوله عليه في سبايا أوطاس: ألا لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن، ولا الحيالي حتى يستبرأن بحيضة"، وهذا يفيد وجوب الاستبراء بسبب إحداث الملك واليد حتى يجب على المشتري من مال الصبي ومن المرأة = والمملوك وممن لا يحل له وطئها الاستبراء، وكذلك إذا كانت المشتراة بكرا لم توطأ؛ لتحقق السبب، ولا يعتد بالحيضة التي اشتراها في أثنائها ولا بالحيضة التي حاضتها بعد الشراء قبل القبض، ولا بالولادة الحاصلة بعده قبل القبض، خلافا لأبي يوسف، ولو وطئها قبل الاستبراء أثم ولا استبراء عليه بعد ذلك. (عيني، فتح)
Chapter on istibra' and other matters. Whoever owns a slave woman, intercourse with her, touching her, and looking at her private parts with desire are forbidden until she completes istibra'. Istibra' linguistically means seeking freedom; legally, seeking freedom of the womb from pregnancy. (Ayni, Fath) 'A slave woman': meaning enjoyment of a slave woman, so excludes a man purchasing his wife. (Fath) 'Intercourse is forbidden' etc.: absolutely, whether one is certain her womb is empty of the seller's semen because her owner was a woman or a child, or she is a virgin or similar, or one is not certain. From Abu Yusuf: if one is certain her womb is empty of the seller's semen, there is no obligation of istibra'. (Mula?) (Miskin?) 'Until she performs istibra': meaning he leaves her until she menstruates once if she is of menstruating age, or one month passes if she is past menopause, or until she delivers if she is pregnant; due to his statement concerning the captives of Autas: 'Lo, pregnant women shall not be approached until they deliver, nor non-pregnant until they perform istibra' by one menstruation.' This indicates the obligation of istibra' due to new ownership and possession, so that it is obligatory for the buyer from the property of a child and from a woman. And the slave and one for whom intercourse is not lawful must also do istibra'. Similarly, if the purchased slave woman is a virgin not previously approached, istibra' is required due to the existence of the cause. And the menstruation during which he purchased her is not counted, nor the menstruation that occurs after purchase but before taking possession, nor the birth that occurs after purchase but before taking possession, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And if he has intercourse with her before istibra', he sins and no istibra' is required after that. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage defines the legal ruling of istibra' (waiting period for a purchased slave woman). The obligation is derived from the hadith of the captives of Autas. The rule is that the buyer must wait one menstrual cycle to ensure the womb is free of the seller's seed. Exceptions: if the seller is a woman or child (so no possibility of pregnancy), or if the slave woman is a virgin never approached, some scholars like Abu Yusuf argue no istibra' is needed if certainty is established. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that istibra' is required in all cases because the cause (new ownership) is present. The istibra' period is one menstruation for menstruating women, one month for post-menopausal, and until delivery for pregnant women. The passage also notes that if intercourse occurs before istibra', it is sinful but no subsequent istibra' is needed. The menstruation at the time of purchase or after purchase but before physical delivery (qabd) does not count. This shows the strictness in ensuring no mixing of lineages.

Key Terms
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): A waiting period for a newly acquired slave woman to ensure her womb is free of the previous owner's pregnancy.
القبض (al-qabd): Physical taking possession of the purchased slave woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration of istibra' for a menstruating slave woman?
A) One month
B) One menstrual cycle
C) Until she delivers
D) Fifty days

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is an obligatory waiting period for the buyer of a slave woman, established by the hadith of Autas, and is required even when the womb is certainly empty.

Harim of a Well: 40 or 60 Cubits?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on well harim distance and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the harim of a well and explain the basis for the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The harim of a well depends on need—Abu Hanifa fixed 40 cubits universally; the Sahibayn specified 40 for hand-drawn and 60 for camel-drawn wells.

Water wells are essential for life and agriculture, and Islamic law protects them with a buffer zone called harim, within which others may not dig. The Hanafi school has an internal difference on the size of this harim. In this lesson, we will examine the two positions, their proofs, and the usul principle that underlies the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
The matn states that the harim of a well is forty cubits from each side. This is the starting point agreed upon by all.
This is the general rule for an ordinary well.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the harim is always forty cubits, regardless of whether the well is for hand-drawing ('atan) or camel-drawing (nadih). He relies on a general hadith that does not differentiate.
His principle: a general, widely accepted hadith takes precedence over a specific, disputed one.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differentiate: for a 'atan well (hand-drawn), the harim is forty cubits; for a nadih well (camel-drawn), it is sixty cubits. They cite a hadith that explicitly gives these measures.
They also argue based on need: a camel-drawn well requires more space for the animal and longer ropes.
4
Examine the proofs
The Sahibayn's hadith is quoted: 'The harim of a spring is 500 cubits, the harim of a 'atan well is 40, and the harim of a nadih well is 60.' Abu Hanifa's proof is a general hadith (not quoted) and the usul principle of preferring general accepted texts over specific disputed ones.
The author analogizes to other cases where this principle was applied.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The difference matters when someone digs a well near another's well. Under Abu Hanifa, the prohibited zone is always 40 cubits; under the Sahibayn, it may be 60 if the well is of the nadih type.
Later Hanafi fatwa tends to favor the Sahibayn as more detailed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فله حريمها أربعون ذراعا من كل جانب، وحريم العين خمس مائة من كل، فمن حفر بئرا في حريمها منع منه. حريم البئر الأولى أربعون ذراعا إلخ ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن تكون البئر للعطن أو للناضح عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: إن كانت للعطن فأربعون ذراعا، وإن كانت للناضح فحريمها ستون ذراعا؛ لقوله عليه: "حريم العين خمسمائة ذراع، وحريم بئر العطن أربعون ذراعا، وحريم بئر الناضح ستون ذراعا"، ولأن استحقاق الحريم باعتبار الحاجة، وحاجة بئر الناضح أكثر؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى موضع يسير فيه الناضح، وهو البعير، وقد يطول الرشاء، وفي بئر العطن يستقى بيده، فلابد من التفاوت بينهما وله ما روينا من غير فصل، ومن أصله أن العام المتفق على قبوله والعمل به مرجح على الخاص المختلف في قبوله والعمل به ولهذا رجح قوله عليه: "ما أخرجته الأرض ففيه العشر" على قوله علي: "ليس فيما دون خمسة أوسق صدقة، وعلى قوله علي: "ليس" في الخضراوات صدقة"، هنا أصحابنا كلهم قوله علي التمر بالتمر مثلا بمثل" على . خبر العرايا. وبئر العطن التي ينزح الماء منها باليد، وبئر الناضح التي ينزح الماء منها بالبعير.
For it, its harim is forty cubits from every side, and the harim of a spring is five hundred from every side. Whoever digs a well in its harim is prohibited from it. The harim of the first well is forty cubits, etc. There is no difference in that between whether the well is for 'atan or for nadih according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if it is for 'atan then forty cubits, and if it is for nadih then its harim is sixty cubits; due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The harim of a spring is five hundred cubits, the harim of a well for 'atan is forty cubits, and the harim of a well for nadih is sixty cubits,' and because entitlement to harim is based on need, and the need of a nadih well is greater because it needs space for the nadih (the camel) to walk, and the rope may be long, while in a well for 'atan one draws water by hand, so there must be a difference between them. And he (Abu Hanifa) has what we narrated without differentiation, and from his principle that a general hadith whose acceptance and practice is agreed upon is given priority over a specific hadith whose acceptance and practice is differed upon. For this reason he gave priority to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whatever the earth produces, one-tenth is due on it' over his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on less than five wasqs' and over his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on vegetables.' Here all our companions give priority to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Dates for dates, like for like' over the hadith of 'araya. The well for 'atan is that from which water is drawn by hand, and the well for nadih is that from which water is drawn by camel.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the harim (protected precinct) of a well. The basic ruling from the matn states that the harim of a well is forty cubits from each side. However, the author then presents the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the positions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to Abu Hanifa, the harim is forty cubits regardless of the type of well. The Sahibayn differentiate: if the well is for 'atan (watering animals by hand), the harim is forty cubits; if it is for nadih (using a camel-driven pulley), the harim is sixty cubits. Their proof is a hadith that specifies different distances for each type, and the reasoning that the need for space is greater for a nadih well because the camel needs room to walk and the rope is longer. Abu Hanifa's proof is a general hadith that does not differentiate, and he applies the principle that a general, agreed-upon hadith takes precedence over a specific, disputed one. He analogizes this to other rulings where general evidence was given priority. The author then clarifies the definitions: a well for 'atan is one where water is drawn by hand, while a well for nadih is one where a camel is used.

Key Terms
حريم (harim): The protected precinct or buffer zone around a well or structure, within which others are prohibited from digging or building.
بئر العطن (bi'r al-'atan): A well from which water is drawn by hand for watering animals.
بئر الناضح (bi'r al-nadih): A well from which water is drawn using a camel-driven pulley mechanism.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the harim of a well used for drawing water by camel (nadih)?
A) 40 cubits
B) 50 cubits
C) 60 cubits
D) 500 cubits

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally differs on well harim; the mufta bihi position distinguishes 40 cubits for hand-drawn and 60 for camel-drawn wells.

Ruling on the Harim of a Spring: 500 Cubits per Side
Ruling on the harim of a spring with proof and measurement details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the harim of a spring, identify its proof, and apply the correct measurement in determining the protected area.

Core Idea
The harim of a spring is 500 cubits from each side, fixed by the Lawgiver beyond human opinion.

The harim (protected zone) around a spring is essential to preserve its water source for irrigation. The Lawgiver has set a specific measurement, but there is a difference among Hanafi scholars on how that measurement is distributed. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the correct position relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: 'Wa harim al-'ayn khams mi'at min kulli janib.' The ruling is a fixed measurement for the protected zone around a spring.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary references a hadith: 'Harim al-'ayn khamsami'at dhira''. The proof is a prophetic statement, transmitted as ahad hadith.
The hadith is not fully quoted here but is considered established.
3
Understand the wisdom
The rationale given: the spring is excavated for agriculture, so it needs a basin to settle water and a channel for flow. The measurement is divine, not based on human reason ('la madkhala lil-ra'y fi al-maqadir').
This emphasizes that fixed measures in sharia are ta'abbudi (devotional).
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
Some scholars interpret the 500 cubits as total from all four sides (125 per side). The text declares 'al-ashah' (the most correct) is 500 cubits per side.
This is an ikhtilaf within the school resolved by tarjih.
5
Apply the correct measurement
Use 500 cubits per side, measured with the 'broken cubit' (6 hand spans). For a spring, any construction or well digging within this zone is prohibited unless it benefits the spring.
The cubit size is specified to ensure consistent application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحريم العين خمس مائة من كل جانب. وحريم العين إلخ لما روينا ولأن العين تستخرج للزراعة، فلابد من وطن يستقر فيه الماء، ومن موضع يجري فيه إلى الزراعة، وقدر الشارع بخمسمائة، ولا مدخل للرأي في المقادير، ثم قيل: الخمسمائة من الجوانب الأربعة، من كل جانب مائة وخمسة وعشرون ذراعا، والأصح أن خمسمائة ذراع من كل جانب، والذراع هو المكسرة، وهو ست قبضات، وكان ذراع الملك سبع قبضات فكسر منه قبضة.
And the harim of a spring is five hundred from every side. The harim of a spring etc. because we narrated and because the spring is excavated for agriculture, so it needs a basin for the water to settle and a channel for it to flow to the fields, and the Lawgiver set it at five hundred, and there is no room for opinion in such measures. Then it is said: the five hundred from the four sides, from each side one hundred and twenty-five cubits, but the correct view is that it is five hundred cubits from each side. The cubit is the broken cubit, which is six hand spans, while the king's cubit was seven hand spans, so one hand span was deducted from it.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the harim of a spring ('ayn). The matn says it is five hundred cubits from each side. The commentary explains the proof: a hadith (which was previously mentioned) and a rational reason that a spring needs space for the water to settle and for irrigation channels. The measurement is divinely ordained and not subject to human reasoning. There is a difference of opinion on interpretation: some say the five hundred cubits are total from all four sides combined (125 each), but the correct view is that it is five hundred cubits from each side. The cubit in question is the 'broken cubit' (mikasra), which is six hand spans, as opposed to the larger royal cubit of seven spans.

Key Terms
عين ('ayn): A spring of water that flows naturally or is excavated.
ذراع مكسرة (dhira' mukasara): A broken cubit, measuring six hand spans, used in legal measurements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct measurement for the harim of a spring according to the text?
A) 125 cubits from each side
B) 500 cubits total
C) 500 cubits from each side
D) 500 cubits from one side only

Key Takeaway
The harim of a spring is a fixed measure of 500 cubits from each side, set by the Lawgiver, and the most correct Hanafi position upholds this per-side interpretation.

Harim of a Canal and Trees: Understanding Protected Zones
Rulings on the harim of an underground canal and planted trees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on the harim of a qanat and trees, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the qanat, and apply the appropriate harim to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The harim protects water and tree rights; for trees it is fixed at five cubits, for canals it depends on water visibility.

In Hanafi law, certain properties enjoy a protective zone known as harim, which prevents others from encroaching. This lesson explores two such zones: the harim of an underground canal (qanat) and the harim of trees planted in dead land. While the latter has a fixed measurement, the former involves a notable internal dispute among the early Hanafi masters. Understanding these rulings is essential for resolving land use conflicts and issuing correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects and their harim rulings
Note the two distinct subjects: the underground canal (qanat) and trees planted in dead land (mawat). The passage provides separate rulings for each.
The canal and trees are treated differently; do not mix them.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the qanat
The passage presents two views: Abu Hanifa holds that a qanat has no harim until water appears on the surface, after which it resembles a spring with 500 cubits. Muhammad al-Shaybani (and reportedly Abu Yusuf) equate it to a well, thus granting a harim from the outset.
This disagreement affects the timing and extent of the protective zone.
3
Confirm the fixed ruling for trees
For trees planted in dead land, the harim is unambiguously fixed at five cubits. This prevents another from planting within that radius.
This ruling is not disputed and applies directly.
4
Apply the rules to practical scenarios
Use the principles to determine, for example, whether a neighbor can plant near a qanat before water appears, or how close they may plant to a tree.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) may lead to different fatwas depending on the mufti's chosen position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللقناة حريم بقدر ما يصلحه. والقناة مجرى الماء تحت الأرض. لم يقدر حريم بشيء يمكن ضبطه، وعن محمد : أنه بمنزلة البئر في استحقاق الحريم. وقيل: هذا قولهما، وعند الإمام: لا حريم له ما لم يظهر الماء على وجه الأرض؛ لأنه نهر في الحقيقة، فتعتبر بالنهر، قالوا: وعند ظهور الماء على الأرض هو بمنزلة عين فوارة، فيقدر حريمها بخمسمائة ذراع. وحريم شجر يغرس في الأرض الموات خمسة أذرع حتى لا يملك غيره أن يغرس شجرا في حريمه.
And for the canal (qanat) there is a harim to the extent that suffices it. The qanat is a water channel underground. No harim was fixed with a determined measure, and from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) it is like a well in entitlement to harim. It is said: this is the view of them (the two companions), while according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it has no harim as long as the water has not appeared on the surface of the earth, because it is in reality a river, so it is treated like a river. They said: when the water appears on the earth, it is like a gushing spring, so its harim is estimated at five hundred cubits. And the harim of trees planted in dead land is five cubits, so that no one else may plant trees in its harim.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage contains rulings on two types of harim. First, the harim of a qanat (an underground water channel). The author notes that there is no fixed measurement; it is whatever suffices for its maintenance. Imam Muhammad equates it to a well, while Abu Hanifa says it has no harim until the water surfaces, at which point it is like a spring with a 500-cubit harim. Second, the harim of trees planted in dead land (mawat) is fixed at five cubits, preventing others from planting trees within that radius. This is a protective zone to ensure the tree can grow without obstruction.

Key Terms
قناة (qanat): An underground channel built to convey water, often from a source to agricultural land.
حريم (harim): A protected zone around a property (e.g., water source, tree) that others must not encroach upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the harim of trees planted in dead land according to the Hanafi school?
A) 10 cubits
B) 5 cubits
C) 500 cubits
D) No harim

Key Takeaway
For trees in dead land, the harim is fixed at five cubits; for canals, it depends on the visibility of water (500 cubits after emergence, none before according to Abu Hanifa, but like a well according to Muhammad).

Large Rivers Are Common Property: The Hanafi Ruling on Shurb
Opening of chapter on water rights: ruling on large rivers not owned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that large natural rivers are not owned, identify the legal reason (illah) based on possession (ihraz), and apply the hadith proof to distinguish between owned and unowned water.

Core Idea
Large flowing rivers are not owned; ownership requires possession, and water's force prevents that.

Water is essential for life and worship. But who owns the rivers? The Hanafi school teaches that large natural rivers like the Tigris and Euphrates belong to no one — they are common to all. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its reasoning, and the prophetic proof that underpins it, helping you understand when water becomes private property and when it remains a shared resource.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject and Ruling
Read the first sentence of the passage: 'Large rivers like the Tigris and Euphrates are not owned.' This is the core ruling. Note that the chapter defines 'shurb' as the share of water.
The ruling applies to natural, flowing rivers, not man-made canals or stored water.
2
Understand the Legal Reason (Illah)
The text states that no one has exclusive control (yad) over these rivers because the force of the water (qahr al-ma') prevents domination. Ownership requires possession (ihraz), and since the current is too strong, possession cannot be established.
This reasoning is based on the Hanafi principle that qabd (physical control) is essential for ownership of movable and immovable property.
3
Enumerate the Permitted Uses
The passage lists specific benefits: watering land, performing wudu, drinking, setting up watermills, and digging canals. All are permissible because the river is unowned.
These uses are mubah (permissible) for everyone.
4
Analyze the Dalil (Proof)
The hadith 'Muslims are partners in three: pasture, water, and fire' is cited. The text clarifies that 'water' here means unpossessed water. Once water is captured (e.g., in a container), it becomes owned by the capturer, just like game.
This hadith is ahad, but accepted as evidence for this ruling.
5
Distinguish Owned vs. Unowned Water
The passage contrasts water in rivers (unowned) with water that is 'ihraz' (possessed). Possessed water cannot be used without permission. This distinction is crucial for daily fiqh.
Example: Water in a bottled container is owned; you cannot take it without the owner's consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الشرب هو نصيب الماء. الأنهار العظام كدجلة والفرات غير مملوكة ولكل أن يسقى أرضه، أي لكل أحد من الناس. غير مملوكة إلخ لأن هذه الأنهار ليس لأحد فيها يد على الخصوص؛ لأن قهر الماء يمنع قهر غيره، فلا يكون محرزا، والملك بالإحراز. ولكل أن يسقي إلخ يعني لما لم تكن هذه الأنهار مملوكة لأحد، فلكل واحد أن يسقي أرضه، ويتوضأ به، ويشربه، وينتصب الرحى عليه ويكري منها نهرا إلى أرضه؛ لقوله عليه: "المسلمون شركاء في ثلاث: الكلأ والماء والنار"، والمراد بالماء ما ليس بمحرز؛ لأنه بالإحراز يخرج من أن يكون مباحا كالصيد إذا أحرز، فلا يجوز لأحد أن ينتفع به إلا بإذنه.
Chapter on shurb. It is the share of water. Large rivers like the Tigris and Euphrates are not owned, and everyone may water his land, meaning every person from the people. Not owned etc. because no one has exclusive control over these rivers, since the force of the water prevents others from dominating it, so it is not possessed, and ownership is through possession. And everyone may water etc. meaning since these rivers are not owned by anyone, each person may water his land, perform wudu with it, drink it, set up a watermill on it, and dig a canal from it to his land; due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Muslims are partners in three: pasture, water, and fire,' and the intended meaning of water is that which is not possessed, because by being possessed it leaves the category of permissible (like game when it is caught), so no one may benefit from it without permission.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on shurb (water rights). It defines shurb as the share of water. The ruling is that large natural rivers (like the Tigris and Euphrates) are not owned by anyone. The reason is that no one can have exclusive possession of such flowing water because its force prevents human control, and ownership is established through possession (ihraz). Therefore, everyone has the right to water their land, perform ablution, drink, set up mills, and dig canals from these rivers. The proof is the hadith that Muslims are partners in three things: grass, water, and fire. The water referred to is unpossessed water; once it is captured and stored, it becomes private property.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): The share or turn of water for irrigation; also the right to use water.
إحراز (ihraz): Possession or acquisition that establishes ownership, typically by physical control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal reason (illah) that large rivers are not owned?
A) Because they are too long to be enclosed.
B) Because no one has exclusive physical control over them due to the force of the water.
C) Because the Prophet designated them as public property.
D) Because they are of equal size to the Tigris and Euphrates.

Key Takeaway
Large natural rivers are common property; ownership requires physical possession, and the hadith confirms partnership in unpossessed water, grass, and fire.
