The Harim of a River: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on harim of a river

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the harim of a river and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.

Core Idea
A river's harim is contested: Abu Hanifa denies it; the Sahibayn affirm it; later Hanafis favor the Sahibayn, especially for small rivers.

This passage addresses whether a river, unlike a well or spring, has a protected area (harim) alongside it. Abu Hanifa holds that a river has no harim unless proven, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, maintain that a river must have a harim for practical needs like walking and dumping mud. The later Hanafi authorities tend to side with the Sahibayn, and there is even a statement of agreement (ittifaq) among the muhaqqiqun. The dispute also extends to the exact measurement of the harim, with Abu Yusuf proposing half the river's width on each side and Muhammad proposing the full width. An important refinement is that the disagreement applies only to large rivers; small rivers that require frequent dredging have a harim by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa states that a river has no harim. A person who digs a river in another's land must provide evidence to claim a harim.
This is the position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Recognize the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say a river does have a harim, specifically a musanna (embankment) for walking and dumping mud. This applies even if dug in dead land.
They base this on practical necessity.
3
Understand the later tarjih
The text reports that muhaqqiqun (verifying scholars) consider the existence of a harim for rivers as agreed upon (bil-ittifaq). The relied-upon view is that a river has a harim.
This tilts the school's fatwa toward the Sahibayn.
4
Compare the two opinions on extent
Even among the Sahibayn, there is a difference: Abu Yusuf says the harim is half the river's width on each side; Muhammad says it is the full width on each side.
The reason: mud may be dumped on one side only.
5
Apply the distinction between large and small rivers
The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn applies only to large rivers that do not need frequent dredging. For small rivers that require regular cleaning, there is consensus (ittifaq) that they have a harim.
This removes the ikhtilaf in many practical cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا حريم للنهر. أي من كان له نهر في أرض غير، فليس له حريم عند أبي حنيفة إلا أن يقيم البيئة على ذلك، وقالا : له مسناة النهر يمشي عليها، ويلقي عليها طينه، وكذا الخلاف لو حفر النهر في الأرض الموات. والمسناة ما يبنى للسيل ليرد الماء عن الأرض. ولا حريم للنهر عند أبي حنيفة وقالا له حريم من الجانبين بقدر إلقاء الطين ونحوه، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وقيل: هذا بالاتفاق، وهو قول المحققين من أصحابنا. ثم اعلم أن الصاحبين وإن اتفقا على أن النهر له حريما، لكن اختلفا في قدره، فأبو يوسف قدره بنصف عرض النهر من الجانبين؛ لأن طينه يلقي في جانبيه، فيقسم عرضه عليهما، وقدره محمد بكل عرضه من كل جانب؛ لأنه قد لا يمكنه إلقاء الطين من جانبيه جميعا، فيقدر بعرضه من كل جانب. وفي "كشف الغوامض": الاختلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه في نهر كبير لا يحتاج فيه إلى كرى في كل حين وأما الأنهار الصغار التي يحتاج إلى كريها أي حفرها في كل وقت، فلها حريم بالاتفاق.
And there is no harim for a river. Meaning: whoever has a river in another's land, he has no harim according to Abu Hanifa unless he provides evidence to that effect. The two companions said: he has a riverbank (musanna) on which to walk and on which to dump its mud. Similarly, the difference holds if he dug the river in dead land. The musanna is what is built for the flood to divert water from the land. There is no harim for a river according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: he has a harim on both sides to the extent of dumping mud and the like, and this was the view of the three (imams). It is said: this is by agreement, and it is the statement of the muhaqqiqun among our scholars. Then know that the two companions, although they agreed that the river has a harim, differed on its extent: Abu Yusuf estimated it as half the width of the river on each side, because its mud is dumped on both sides, so the width is divided between them. Muhammad estimated it as the full width on each side, because it may not be possible to dump the mud from both sides, so it is estimated as its width on each side. And in 'Kashf al-Ghawamid': the difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions is regarding a large river that does not need dredging every so often. As for small rivers that need dredging (i.e., digging) every time, they have a harim by agreement.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on shurb with a dispute over whether a river (nahr) has a harim. According to Abu Hanifa, there is no harim for a river; if someone digs a river in another's land, he must provide evidence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does have a harim, specifically a musanna (embankment) for walking and dumping mud. This difference also applies if the river is dug in dead land. Some later scholars (muhaqqiqun) say there is agreement on the existence of a harim. Even among the Sahibayn, they differ on the extent: Abu Yusuf says the harim is half the river's width on each side (since mud is dumped on both sides), while Muhammad says it is the full width on each side (in case dumping on one side is difficult). The text clarifies that this dispute applies only to large rivers that do not require frequent dredging; for small rivers that need regular cleaning, there is consensus that they have a harim.

Key Terms
مسناة (musanna): An embankment or bank built along a river to walk on and to dump excavated mud.
حريم (harim): A protected buffer zone around a water source (well, spring, river) where no one else may dig or build without permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full width of the river on each side
B) Half the width of the river on each side
C) No harim at all
D) 500 cubits on each side

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately grants a river a harim based on practical need, with the precise extent differing among the Sahibayn and depending on the size of the river.

Changing Division of Water Shares and Prohibiting Diversion Without Consent
Rulings on altering established water division and prohibiting diversion without consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on changing an established water division and explain the prohibition on diverting water to another land without consent.

Core Idea
An established water division by sluices cannot be changed to days; diverting water to another land is prohibited without consent.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, with its extensive commentary, addresses two key issues in shared water rights: altering the method of distribution and taking water to a different plot. The central principle is that once a division is fixed, it cannot be unilaterally changed, even if no harm is caused. Any alteration requires the unanimous consent of all partners.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage prohibits two acts: 1) changing the division of water shares from sluices to days, and 2) diverting one's water right to another land. Determine the ruling (haram) and the underlying reasoning.
2
Trace the condition of the old division
Note that the prohibition applies when the division has already been made by sluices. The old arrangement is preserved because the right is clear. Understand that this is a protective measure.
3
Distinguish between private canal and main river
The text distinguishes between a private canal (nahr khaas) and the main river (al-nahr al-a'zam). In a private canal, no one may alter a sluice even without harm, because the partnership is specific. In the main river, one may initially dig a canal, but altering sluices in a shared canal is even more prohibited.
4
Understand the harm and false claims rationale
The prohibition on diverting water to another land is based on the fear of a false prescriptive claim. Closing a sluice to prevent flooding is also prohibited if it harms another partner. Recognize that harm prevention is a key principle.
5
Recognize the requirement of consent
All such dispositions require the consent of all partners. Even after a lease, other partners may revoke it because the act is a voluntary gift (tabarru'), which is non-binding until executed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو يقسم بالأيام، وقد وقعت القسمة بالكوى، أو يسوق شربه إلى أرض له أخرى أي ليس لأحدهم أن يقسم بالأيام والحال أنه قد وقعت القسمة بالكوى؛ لأن القديم يترك على حاله، لظهور الحق فيه، ولو كان لكل واحد منهم كوى مسماة في نهر خاص، لم يكن لواحد منهم أن يغير كوة، وإن كان لا يضر بأهله؛ لأن الشركة خاصة، بخلاف ما إذا كان الكوى في النهر الأعظم؛ لأن لكل واحد منهم أن يشق نهرا منه ابتداء، فكان الكوى بالطريق الأولى، ولو أراد الأعلى من الشريكين في نهر خاص، وفيه كوى بينهما، أن يسد بعضها دفعا لفيض الماء عن أرضه، ليس له ذلك؛ للإضرار بالآخر. (فتح الله المعين) وقد وقعت: الجملة حالية يعني والحال أنه قد وقعت بالكوى إلخ الكوى بكسر الكاف، ويجوز فيه المد والقصر، وهو جمع كوة – بالفتح - وهو النقب، وقد تضم الكاف في المفرد والجمع، ويستعار لمفاتيح الماء إلى المزارع والجداول فيقال: كوى النهر. (ملا مسكين، عيني) أو يسوق شربه إلخ أي ليس لأحد أن يسوق شربه إلى أرض أخرى ليس لها أي للأرض الأخرى في النهر شرب؛ لأنه إذا فعل ذلك يخشى أن يدعي حق الشرب لها من هذا النهر مع الأولى إذا تقادم العهد. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٣/٢] ويستدل على ذلك بالحفر وإجراء الماء فيه إليها. (تكملة بلا رضائهم إلخ : متعلق بالجميع أي ليس لأحد من الشركاء تلك التصرفات المذكورة في النهر المشترك إلا برضاء الشركاء، ولهم نقضه بعد الإجارة، ولورثتهم من بعدهم؛ لأن هذا تبرع كما حققه الزيلعي، والتبرعات غير لازمة. (فتح بزيادة من المحشي)
Or he divides by days, while division has already been made by sluices (kowa), or he conveys his water right to another land of his – meaning none of them may divide by days when division has already been made by sluices, because the old arrangement is left as it is, due to the clarity of the right. If each of them has designated sluices in a private canal, none may change a sluice even if it does not harm his people, because the partnership is specific. This is unlike the case of sluices in the main river, because each may initially dig a canal from it, so the sluice is a fortiori. If the upstream partner in a private canal with sluices between them wants to close some to prevent flooding of his land, he may not do so because it harms the other. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in) 'And it has occurred' – the sentence is circumstantial, meaning while it has occurred by sluices. 'al-Kowa' with kasr on the kaf, it is permissible to lengthen and shorten it; it is the plural of 'kuwwa' (with fatha) meaning an opening, and the kaf may be damma in singular and plural; it is used metaphorically for water outlets to farms and streams, so one says 'kowa of the river'. (Mulla Miskin, Ayni) 'Or he conveys his water right' – meaning none may convey his water right to another land that has no water right in the river, because if he does so, it is feared that he might claim the water right for it from this river along with the first if time passes. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/393] This is evidenced by digging and running water through it. (Completion) 'Without their consent' – it relates to all, meaning none of the partners may engage in the mentioned dispositions in the shared canal except with the consent of the partners, and they may revoke it after lease, and their inheritors after them, because this is a voluntary act (tabarru') as verified by al-Zayla'i, and voluntary acts are not binding. (Fath with addition from the annotator)
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, expanded by commentary. The first ruling addresses changing the method of dividing water shares: if water shares have already been allocated by specific sluices (kuwan), it is not permissible to change to a division by days (i.e., time-based rotation). The old division is left intact because the right is established. If each partner has a designated sluice in a private canal, no one may alter their sluice even if it does not harm others, because the partnership is specific to that canal. However, in a main river (al-nahr al-a'zam), each partner may initially dig a new canal, so altering a sluice in such a shared canal is even more prohibited. If one partner upstream wants to close some sluices to prevent flooding, he cannot because it harms the other. The second ruling is about diverting water to another land: no partner may convey his water right to a different plot that has no established right in that river, because over time it could lead to a claim of prescriptive right. The final part explains that any such changes require the consent of all partners, and even after a lease, the other partners can revoke it, as it is a non-binding voluntary act.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): A water right or share in a water source for irrigation.
كوة (kuwwa / kowa): An opening or sluice in a canal that regulates water flow to specific lands; plural: كوى (kowa).
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act or gift without compensation; not binding once revoked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if water shares have already been divided by specific sluices (kowa), can one partner change to a division by days?
A) Yes, if it does not harm others.
B) Yes, with the consent of all partners.
C) No, because the old division is left as it is due to the clarity of the right.
D) No, never, even with consent.

Key Takeaway
The old division is left as is; no partner may change it or divert water without consent.

8 min
Conditions of Valid Possession in Pledge and Takhliya as Possession
Defines the conditions for valid possession (qabd) in a pledge contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid possession (qabd) in a pledge contract and explain why takhliya suffices as possession according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Takhliya (vacating) counts as valid possession in pledge; the contract becomes binding only upon qabd.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the conditions that the pledged item must meet for possession to be valid, and it clarifies that vacating (takhliya) by the pledgor is sufficient to transfer liability. Understanding these conditions is essential for determining when a pledge becomes binding and who bears the risk of loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a pledge contract (rahn). The ruling: it is concluded by offer and acceptance but becomes binding (yatimmu) only upon possession (qabd).
Possession is a condition for bindingness, not for initial validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is the Quranic verse: 'فَرِهَانٌ مَقْبُوضَةٌ' (Al-Baqarah 2:283).
The word 'maqbūḍah' (possessed) modifies 'rihān', indicating that possession is integral.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The adjective 'maqbūḍah' ties the term 'rihān' to possession, so the contract is not completed except by qabd. This is a condition (shart) derived from the text.
The dalala is zanni because the imperative form is indirect.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds that the pledge is binding by the contract alone, like sale and lease. The Hanafi response is that the Quranic text is specific and overrides qiyas.
The thamarah al-khilaf: who bears loss before possession.
5
Understand the expansion on conditions of possession
The pledged item must be: محوزا (collected, e.g., dates cut from trees), مفرغا (emptied, e.g., land without crops), مميزا (distinguished, not shared). Takhliya (vacating) by the pledgor constitutes qabd, and Abu Yusuf's narrower view is overruled.
Takhliya is the pledgor's act; it is considered sufficient because it removes obstacles.

وقبضه محوزا مفرغا مميزا، والتخلية فيه، وفي البيع قبض وله أن يرجع عن الرهن احتراز عن المشغول ما لم يقبضه، وهو مضمون المرقمن الرهن بعد يصح القبض بين الراهن والمرتمن بين المبيع والمشتري أي يجوز للراهن : وقبضه إلخ: هذا عطف على قوله: "إيجاب" أي لزم الرهن بقبض، ووقع في أكثر الشروح: "ويتم بقبضه"، وهذا هو المطابق لما في "العيني" وغيره من قوله: "وينعقد بإيجاب" إلخ، وهو الصحيح باعتبار المعنى إذا كان ما في "العيني" هو الصحيح، وأما على ما في النسخ المطبوعة، فيصح قوله : "وقبضه" باعتبار المعنى، وإن لم يصح معنى قوله: "ولزم بإيجاب" فافهم واحفظ، وحاصل المعنى: أن الرهن يتم بقبض المرهون حال كونه محوزا أي مجموعا، احترز به عن رهن التمر على رؤوس النخل والزرع في الأرض وحال كونه مفرغا، احترز به عن رهن النخل بدون الثمر، والأرض بدون الزرع، وحال كونه مميزا، احترز به عن الشيوع، وفي رمز الحقائق: وقال مالك: يلزم بنفس العقد كالبيع والإجارة، ولنا: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَرِهَانٌ مَقْبُوضَةٌ﴾، علقه بالقبض، فلا يتم إلا به. [٤٠٤/٢] والتخلية فيه إلخ: يعني أن التخلية بين الشيء المرهون والمرتهن في الرهن وبين المبيع والمشتري في حكم القبض حتى إذ وجدت من الراهن بحضرة المرتهن ولم يأخذه، فضاع ضمن المرتمن؛ لأن هذا هو غاية ما يقدر عليه، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه لا في المنقول إلا بالنقل وبه قال أحمد قال الشارح الزيلعي والصواب أن التخلية تسليم؛ لأنه عبارة عن رفع الموانع من القبض، وهو فعل المسلم دون المتسلم والقبض فعل المتسلم، قلت: إذا كانت التخلية تسليما، فمن ضرورته الحكم بالقبض سواء وجد القبض حقيقة أو لا، فالشيخ حليه ذكر الغاية التي يبنى عليها الحكم؛ لأنه هو المقصود (عيني فتح
And its possession must be held, emptied, distinguished, and vacating (takhliya) counts as possession in it, while in sale [possession is different], and he may revoke the pledge as long as it has not been possessed. ... The summary: the pledge is completed by possession of the pledged item while it is held, i.e., collected—precaution against pledging dates on top of palm trees and crops in the land—and while it is emptied—precaution against pledging palm trees without fruit and land without crops—and while it is distinguished—precaution against common ownership. In Ramz al-Haqa'iq: Malik said: it is binding by the contract itself like sale and lease. Our proof: Allah's statement: 'Then a pledged property [held] in possession' (2:283), He tied it to possession, so it is not completed except by it. And takhliya in it: i.e., vacating between the pledged item and the pledgee in pledge and between the sold item and the buyer in the ruling of possession, such that if it occurs from the pledgor in the presence of the pledgee and he does not take it and it is lost, the pledgee is liable...
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage expands on the conditions of valid possession (qabd) for a pledge. The author explains that the matn's phrase 'held, emptied, distinguished' means the pledged item must be collected (e.g., not scattered fruit on trees), emptied of other items (e.g., land without crops), and distinguished from shared property. Takhliya (vacating by the pledgor) is considered equivalent to physical possession in pledge and sale, as it is the maximum the pledgor can do. The Hanafi proof is the Quranic verse 'farihanun maqbūḍah', which conditions validity on possession, refuting Malik's view that the contract is binding without possession. Abu Yusuf's opinion that only movable property requires transfer is noted but the relied-upon view is that takhliya suffices.

Key Terms
محوزا (maḥwzan): Collected or gathered; the pledged item must be physically gathered (e.g., dates on trees are not considered possessed unless cut and collected).
مفرغا (mufarraghan): Emptied; the item must be free from other attached items (e.g., land without crops, trees without fruit).
مميزا (mumayyazan): Distinguished; the item must be separate from shared property, not in common ownership.
التخلية (al-takhliyah): Vacating by the pledgor; removing all obstacles between the pledgee and the item, so that the pledgee can take possession if he wishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a pledge contract if the pledgor merely vacates the item (takhliya) but the pledgee does not physically take it?
A) The contract is void.
B) The contract is binding and the pledgee is liable for the item.
C) The contract is concluded but not binding until physical transfer.
D) The contract is binding only if the item is movable and physically transferred.

Key Takeaway
The pledge contract becomes binding only upon valid possession, which requires the item to be collected, emptied, and distinguished; takhliya by the pledgor constitutes possession.

Priority of Father's Executor over Grandfather
Ruling on who manages child's property: father's executor vs grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the priority of the father's executor over the grandfather, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this dispute.

Core Idea
The father's explicit choice of executor outweighs the grandfather's default substitution.

When a father dies leaving minor children, the question arises: who should manage their property? The Hanafi school gives priority to the executor appointed by the father, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues the grandfather is more entitled. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the father's executor is more entitled than the grandfather to manage the minor's property.
The text begins: 'ووصي الأب أحق بمال الطفل من الجد'.
2
Identify the opposing view
State the Shafi'i position: the grandfather is more entitled, even when an executor exists.
Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: the Law places him in the father's position.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the rational proof: the father's appointment transfers guardianship, and his choice indicates better care.
The text says: 'لأن اختياره مع علمه بالجد يدل على أن تصرفه أنظر لأولاده'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: if an executor exists, he manages; otherwise the grandfather does. For Shafi'i, grandfather always manages.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is the executor's priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووصي الأب أحق بمال الطفل من الجد، فإن لم يوص الأب، فالجد كالأب. وقال الشافعي له الجدّ أحق؛ لأن الشرع أقامه مقام الأب عند عدمه حتى أحرز ميراثه فيتقدم على وصيه ولنا أن ولاية الأب تنتقل إليه بالإيصاء، فكانت ولايته قائمة معنى، فيقدم عليه كالأب نفسه؛ لأن اختياره مع علمه بالجد يدل على أن تصرفه أنظر لأولاده من تصرف الجد. فالجد كالأب: يعني إن لم يوص الأب فالجد كالأب؛ لأنه أقرب الناس إليه، حتى ملك الإنكاح دون الوصي.
And the father's executor is more entitled to the child's property than the grandfather. If the father did not appoint an executor, then the grandfather is like the father. Al-Shafi'i said: The grandfather is more entitled because the Law places him in the position of the father in his absence—even inheriting from him—so he takes precedence over the executor. Our proof: The father's guardianship transfers to the executor through appointment, so his guardianship remains in meaning, so he is preferred like the father himself, because his choice, despite knowing the grandfather, indicates that his management is more considerate for his children than the grandfather's management. "So the grandfather is like the father": meaning if the father did not appoint an executor, the grandfather is like the father because he is the closest relative, to the extent that he has authority in marriage without the executor.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding who has priority over a minor child's property: the father's appointed executor or the grandfather. The Hanafi position is that the father's executor is preferred, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the grandfather is more entitled. The Hanafi proof is based on reason: the father, knowing the grandfather's existence, still chose another person as executor, which shows that he considered that person's management better for his children. Thus, the executor's authority is a continuation of the father's authority. The passage also clarifies that if the father dies without appointing an executor, the grandfather steps into his role as the closest relative, with authority even in marriage matters.

Key Terms
وصي الأب (wasi al-abb): The person appointed by the father as executor over his minor children's affairs.
الجد (al-jadd): The paternal grandfather of the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who has priority in managing a minor child's property after the father's death?
A) The maternal uncle
B) The grandfather
C) The father's appointed executor
D) The mother

Key Takeaway
The father's executor is preferred over the grandfather because the father's explicit appointment indicates better care, and the executor's authority derives directly from the father.

Definition and Signs of the Khuntha (Hermaphrodite)
Defining the khuntha and its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of khuntha (clear and ambiguous) and state the Hanafi rule for determining gender when signs conflict.

Core Idea
A khuntha is classified as a woman if intercourse is possible via the female organ; otherwise, conflicting signs leave the person ambiguous.

This lesson introduces the concept of the khuntha (hermaphrodite) in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding the definition and the signs that determine gender is essential before moving to the practical rulings that apply to the ambiguous type. We will learn how the Hanafi school distinguishes between a clear khuntha and an ambiguous one (khuntha mushkil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of khuntha
First, note that the passage distinguishes between a khuntha whose gender is clear (either male or female based on the possibility of intercourse) and one whose gender is ambiguous (when no sign appears or signs conflict).
The clear type is ruled as a woman if the female organ allows intercourse; otherwise, the person is considered a man based on other signs.
2
Understand the primary sign for a khuntha being a woman
The text states: 'إذا أمكن وطيه فامرأة' – if intercourse through the female organ is possible, the person is considered a woman. This is the key determinant for classification.
This sign overrides other potential indicators.
3
Recognize the condition for ambiguity
If no sign appears after puberty, or if signs conflict (e.g., menstruation and beard growth), the person is classified as a khuntha mushkil (ambiguous). The commentator refutes the idea that ambiguity cannot persist after puberty.
Examples of conflicting signs include both menstruation and facial hair.
4
Learn additional sign reported from al-Hasan
The passage mentions a method of counting ribs: the male has one more rib than the female. This is an additional sign used to resolve ambiguity, though it is not the primary criterion.
This rib-counting method is attributed to al-Hasan al-Basri.

Book of the Khuntha. Rulings of the Khuntha. Or if intercourse with him is possible, then [he is] a woman. And if no sign appears or they conflict, then [he is] ambiguous. He stands between the row of men and women in prayer. And an enslaved woman is purchased for him to circumcise him. If he has no wealth, then from the public treasury. Then she is bought to be sold. And for him is the lesser of the two shares in inheritance. (Commentary): 'Or if intercourse is possible, etc.' means he is a woman, so his ruling is the ruling of women; because this is a sign of women. 'And if no sign appears, etc.' and what was said that after puberty it is inconceivable for him to remain ambiguous was rejected in Hashiyat al-Shalabi unless [it is said] in the majority or [the signs] conflict. 'Or they conflict, etc.' means the signs conflict, such as if he menstruates or grows a beard, or he engages in intercourse and is penetrated. 'Then ambiguous' means he is an ambiguous khuntha due to lack of preference. And from al-Hasan: that his ribs are counted, for the man's rib exceeds the woman's rib by one. 'He stands, etc.': This is the ruling of the ambiguous khuntha: he stands between the row of men and women; he gives precedence to women due to the possibility of being a man. If he prays with women, he repeats his prayer for that reason; if he prays with men, he repeats three prayers: the one to his right, the one to his left, and the one behind him, as a precaution due to the possibility of being a woman. It is recommended that he prays with a headcover due to the possibility of being a woman; and if he is a free adult, it is obligatory upon him. 'And an enslaved woman is purchased for him, etc.': means with his wealth, because it is permissible for his female slave to look at him absolutely if he is male, and out of necessity if he is female. It is disliked that a man circumcises him due to the possibility of being female, or a woman due to the possibility of being male. The precaution is as we mentioned because it is not forbidden on the assumption that he is male, nor on the assumption that he is female; because the look of one gender to another is lighter. 'The public treasury, etc.': because the public treasury is prepared for the exigencies of Muslims. It enters his ownership to the extent of need, which is circumcision. When she circumcises him, she is sold and her price is returned to the public treasury. If he marries a woman, then she circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is permissible; because if he is male, the marriage is valid; if she is female, the look of one gender to the other is lighter. Then they are separated due to the possibility that she is female, so no marriage between them; and he divorces due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage is valid between them; thus separation occurs. Then she observes waiting period if he had seclusion with her, as a precaution. In al-Dhakhira: If the ambiguous khuntha says 'I am male' or 'female', his statement is accepted because a person is trustworthy regarding himself; the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the opposite of what he said is not known.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage defines the khuntha (hermaphrodite) and provides rulings for the 'ambiguous' type (khuntha mushkil). It begins by stating that if one has both male and female reproductive organs but intercourse through the female organ is possible, the person is considered a woman. If no clear sign appears after puberty or signs conflict (e.g., menstruation and beard growth), the person remains ambiguous. The commentator clarifies that some scholars thought ambiguity could not persist after puberty but this is refuted unless the ambiguity is rare. In prayer, the ambiguous khuntha stands between the rows of men and women, leaning towards women but avoiding being in the pure row of either. He must repeat prayers prayed in either row as a precaution. He should also cover his head in prayer due to the possibility of being female. For circumcision, a female slave is bought (with his money or public treasury) to perform the circumcision, because direct touch by a man or woman is disliked due to the possibility of opposite gender. The slave is then sold and the money returned to the treasury. If he marries a woman and the slave circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is considered a valid divorce regardless of his gender, and if seclusion occurred, the woman must observe an 'iddah (waiting period). Finally, the ambiguous khuntha's own statement about his gender is accepted as he is trustworthy about himself.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A person with both male and female reproductive organs or an unclear gender
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose gender is ambiguous due to lack or conflict of signs
وطء (wat'): Sexual intercourse; here meaning the possibility of penetration through the female organ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes a khuntha considered a woman?
A) Having breasts
B) The possibility of intercourse through the female organ
C) Menstruation
D) Having fewer ribs

Key Takeaway
The gender of a khuntha is determined by signs; if intercourse through the female organ is possible, the person is a woman; if signs are absent or conflict, the person is a khuntha mushkil.

Prayer, Circumcision, and Marriage of the Khuntha Mushkil
Rulings for the ambiguous khuntha in prayer, circumcision, marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for the ambiguous khuntha (khuntha mushkil) regarding congregational prayer, circumcision procedure, and marriage/divorce.

Core Idea
The ambiguous khuntha must stand between rows in prayer, be circumcised by a female slave, and his statement about his gender is accepted.

Once a person is identified as a khuntha mushkil (ambiguous), specific precautionary rulings come into effect to accommodate both possibilities. This lesson covers the most important practical applications: where he stands in congregational prayer, how his circumcision is performed to avoid unlawful looking or touching, and the validity of his marriage and divorce. These rulings are based on the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) to ensure validity regardless of the true gender.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prayer placement
The khuntha mushkil stands between the rows of men and women, slightly closer to the women's side to avoid being in a pure row of either gender. He must repeat prayers prayed in a pure row.
He also wears a headcover (qina') as a precaution because of the possibility of being female.
2
Learn the circumcision ruling
A female slave is purchased (with his money or from the public treasury) to perform the circumcision, because it is disliked for a man or woman to directly touch him due to the possibility of opposite gender.
After circumcision, the slave is sold and the money returned to the treasury.
3
Examine the marriage and divorce scenario
If the khuntha marries a woman and then divorces her after the slave circumcises him, the divorce is valid in either case. If seclusion occurred, the woman must observe 'iddah.
This ruling ensures that regardless of the true gender, the separation is effective.
4
Know the acceptance of his own statement
If the khuntha mushkil declares his gender (male or female), his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy about himself unless evidence contradicts.
This is from al-Dhakhira and is the relied-upon position.

فامرأة إلخ: أي فهو امرأة، فحكمه حكم النساء؛ رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٢] لأن هذه من علامات النساء. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٠٠/٩] وإن لم تظهر علامة إلخ وما قيل من أنه بعد البلوغ لا يتصور بقاؤه مشكلا، رده في "حاشية الشلبي" إلا إذا أريد به الغالب أو تعارضت إلخ : أي تعارضت العلامات مثل ما إذا حاض، أو خرجت له لحية، أو يأتي ويؤتى رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٢] فمشكل: أي فهو خنثى مشكل؛ لعدم المرجح، وعن الحسن: أنه تعد أضلاعه، فإن ضلع الرجل يزيد على ضلع المرأة بواحدة. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٢] فيقف إلخ: هذا هو حكم الخنثى المشكل أي فيقف بين صف الرجال والنساء، فيقدم على النساء؛ لاحتمال كونه رجلا، فإن صلى معهن أعاد صلاته لذلك، وإن صلى مع الرجال أعاد الصلاة ثلاثة الذي عن يمينه، والذي عن يساره، والذي خلفه احتياطا؛ لاحتمال كونه ،امرأة ويستحب أن يصلي بقناع لاحتمال كونه امرأة، ولو كان بالغا حرا يجب عليه ذلك رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٢] وتبتاع له أمة إلخ: يعني بماله؛ لأنه يجوز لمملوكته النظر إليه مطلقا إن كان ذكرا وللضرورة إن كان أنثى، ويكره أن يختنه رجل؛ لاحتمال أنه أنثى أو امرأة؛ لاحتمال أنه ذكر، فكان الاحتياط فيما ذكرنا؛ لأنه لا يحرم على تقدير أن يكون ذكرا، وعلى تقدير أن يكون أنثى؛ لأن نظر الجنس إلى الجنس أخف. (تكملة) بيت المال إلخ لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين، فيدخل في ملكه بقدر الحاجة، وهي الختان، فإذا ختنته تباع، ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فلو تزوج امرأة ثم ختنته، ثم طلقها جاز؛ لأنه إن كان ذكرا صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى، فنظر الجنس أخف، ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه أنثى، فلا نكاح بينهما، ويطلق لاحتمال أنه ذكر، فيصح النكاح بينهما، فتحصل الفرقة به، ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطا، وفي "الذخيرة": إن قال الخنثى المشكل: أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله؛ لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه، والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٢]
Book of the Khuntha. Rulings of the Khuntha. Or if intercourse with him is possible, then [he is] a woman. And if no sign appears or they conflict, then [he is] ambiguous. He stands between the row of men and women in prayer. And an enslaved woman is purchased for him to circumcise him. If he has no wealth, then from the public treasury. Then she is bought to be sold. And for him is the lesser of the two shares in inheritance. (Commentary): 'Or if intercourse is possible, etc.' means he is a woman, so his ruling is the ruling of women; because this is a sign of women. 'And if no sign appears, etc.' and what was said that after puberty it is inconceivable for him to remain ambiguous was rejected in Hashiyat al-Shalabi unless [it is said] in the majority or [the signs] conflict. 'Or they conflict, etc.' means the signs conflict, such as if he menstruates or grows a beard, or he engages in intercourse and is penetrated. 'Then ambiguous' means he is an ambiguous khuntha due to lack of preference. And from al-Hasan: that his ribs are counted, for the man's rib exceeds the woman's rib by one. 'He stands, etc.': This is the ruling of the ambiguous khuntha: he stands between the row of men and women; he gives precedence to women due to the possibility of being a man. If he prays with women, he repeats his prayer for that reason; if he prays with men, he repeats three prayers: the one to his right, the one to his left, and the one behind him, as a precaution due to the possibility of being a woman. It is recommended that he prays with a headcover due to the possibility of being a woman; and if he is a free adult, it is obligatory upon him. 'And an enslaved woman is purchased for him, etc.': means with his wealth, because it is permissible for his female slave to look at him absolutely if he is male, and out of necessity if he is female. It is disliked that a man circumcises him due to the possibility of being female, or a woman due to the possibility of being male. The precaution is as we mentioned because it is not forbidden on the assumption that he is male, nor on the assumption that he is female; because the look of one gender to another is lighter. 'The public treasury, etc.': because the public treasury is prepared for the exigencies of Muslims. It enters his ownership to the extent of need, which is circumcision. When she circumcises him, she is sold and her price is returned to the public treasury. If he marries a woman, then she circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is permissible; because if he is male, the marriage is valid; if she is female, the look of one gender to the other is lighter. Then they are separated due to the possibility that she is female, so no marriage between them; and he divorces due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage is valid between them; thus separation occurs. Then she observes waiting period if he had seclusion with her, as a precaution. In al-Dhakhira: If the ambiguous khuntha says 'I am male' or 'female', his statement is accepted because a person is trustworthy regarding himself; the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the opposite of what he said is not known.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage defines the khuntha (hermaphrodite) and provides rulings for the 'ambiguous' type (khuntha mushkil). It begins by stating that if one has both male and female reproductive organs but intercourse through the female organ is possible, the person is considered a woman. If no clear sign appears after puberty or signs conflict (e.g., menstruation and beard growth), the person remains ambiguous. The commentator clarifies that some scholars thought ambiguity could not persist after puberty but this is refuted unless the ambiguity is rare. In prayer, the ambiguous khuntha stands between the rows of men and women, leaning towards women but avoiding being in the pure row of either. He must repeat prayers prayed in either row as a precaution. He should also cover his head in prayer due to the possibility of being female. For circumcision, a female slave is bought (with his money or public treasury) to perform the circumcision, because direct touch by a man or woman is disliked due to the possibility of opposite gender. The slave is then sold and the money returned to the treasury. If he marries a woman and the slave circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is considered a valid divorce regardless of his gender, and if seclusion occurred, the woman must observe an 'iddah (waiting period). Finally, the ambiguous khuntha's own statement about his gender is accepted as he is trustworthy about himself.

Key Terms
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose gender is ambiguous due to lack or conflict of signs
أمة (ama): An enslaved female; purchased specifically for circumcision of the khuntha
إحتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution; the principle of adopting the safer legal option to ensure validity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is the circumcision of a khuntha mushkil performed according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) A male surgeon circumcises him
B) He circumcises himself
C) A female slave circumcises him
D) It is not required

Key Takeaway
The ambiguous khuntha's prayer, circumcision, and marriage are governed by precaution: he stands between rows, is circumcised by a female slave, and his marriage/divorce is valid under both gender possibilities.

When Does a Wet Najis Cloth Transfer Impurity to a Dry Cloth?
Ruling on impurity transfer via dampness with condition of squeezability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a dry cloth becomes najis by contact with a wet najis cloth and identify the key condition of squeeze-able moisture.

Core Idea
No impurity transfer without squeeze-able moisture — mere dampness does not transmit najasa.

Imagine a wet najis cloth wrapped in a dry clean cloth. Does the clean cloth become impure? The Hanafi school says: not unless you can squeeze out liquid. This lesson explains the precise condition distinguishing harmless dampness from impurity-transferring wetness, along with important exceptions for different types of impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is wrapping a wet najis cloth in a dry clean cloth. The ruling: the clean cloth remains pure (tahir) if moisture appears but cannot be squeezed out.
The ruling hinges on whether liquid can be extracted by pressure.
2
Distinguish between Types of Impurity
Note that the ruling applies only when the wet cloth became najis due to 'aradiyya impurity (acquired, e.g., water that touched impurity). It does not apply to 'ayniyya impurity (the substance itself, like urine).
'Ayniyya impurity requires stricter treatment.
3
Apply the Condition of Squeezability
The key condition is that no liquid can be squeezed out (la yan'asir). The text notes variant wording: la yaseel (does not flow). Both indicate significant moisture.
If liquid can be squeezed or flows, impurity transfers.
4
Extend to Analogous Scenarios
The passage gives analogous cases: a wet cloth on a dry najis rope — no transfer; washing foot and walking on najis ground — no transfer if foot dry? Actually the text says opposite for wet ground. Understand each scenario's moisture condition.
The principle is consistent: transfer requires transferable moisture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لُفَّ ثوب نجس رطب في ثوب طاهر يابس، فظهر رطوبته على ثوب طاهر لكن لا ينعصر لو عصر، لا ينجس. نجس رطب تنجس بماء نجاسته عرضية، فخرج ما لو تنجس بعين النجاسة كالبول. (طائي) لا ينعصر إلخ أقول: هكذا هو في جميع نسخ "الكنز" الموجودة عندي، وقد وقع في جميع شروحه مثل العيني والطائي وملا مسكين والتكملة مكان "لا ينعصر" "لا يسيل"، فاحفظ. لا ينجس إلخ أي لا يتنجس الثوب الطاهر؛ لأنه إذا لم يتقاطر من الثوب النجس بالعصر لا ينفصل منه شيء، وإنما يبتل ما يجاوره بالنداوة، وبذلك لا يتنجس، وعلى هذا إذا نشر الثوب المبلول على حبل نجس وهو يابس لا يتنجس الثوب، أو غسل رجله ومشى على أرض نجسة، أو نام على فراش فعرق ولم يظهر أثره، لا ينجس، ولو مشى على أرض رطبة نجسة ورجله يابس تتنجس. (عيني، فتح)
A wet najis cloth wrapped in a dry clean cloth, if its moisture appears on the clean cloth but does not drip if squeezed, it does not make it najis. Wet najis: najis by water that is ritually impure (najasa 'aradiyya), excluding najasa 'ayniyya like urine. (Tai) 'la yan'asir' etc. I say: Thus it is in all copies of al-Kanz I have, and in all its commentaries like al-Ayni, al-Tai, Mulla Miskin, and al-Takmila, instead of 'la yan'asir' it is 'la yaseel', so memorize. It does not become najis: i.e., the clean cloth does not become najis because if nothing separates from the najis cloth by squeezing, nothing separates from it, and only the adjacent part becomes damp, and by that it does not become najis. Similarly, if a wet cloth is spread on a dry najis rope, the cloth does not become najis; or if one washes his foot and walks on najis ground; or sleeps on a bed and sweats without trace, it does not become najis. But if he walks on wet najis ground with a dry foot, it becomes najis. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage gives a detailed ruling on the transmission of ritual impurity (najasa) through moisture. The scenario: a wet cloth that is najis is wrapped in a dry clean cloth, and moisture from the wet cloth appears on the dry cloth but cannot be squeezed out (i.e., no liquid can be extracted by pressure). In this case, the dry cloth does NOT become najis. The reasoning is that impurity only transfers when a significant amount of liquid separates; mere dampness (nadaawah) does not transfer impurity. This ruling applies when the wet cloth became najis due to 'aradiyya (secondary impurity, e.g., water that came into contact with impurity but is not itself the substance). It does not apply to 'ayniyya (the impurity itself, like urine). The commentators note variant wording in texts: some say 'la yan'asir' (does not squeeze) and others say 'la yaseel' (does not flow). The lesson also gives analogous scenarios: a wet cloth on a dry najis rope does not become najis; but if the foot is dry and the ground is wet najis, the foot becomes najis because moisture transfers.

Key Terms
ينعصر (yan'asir): To be squeezed out; if liquid cannot be squeezed, no impurity transfer.
عرضية (aradiyya): Impurity that is not the substance itself but acquired (e.g., water that touched najasa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a dry clean cloth become najis if wrapped around a wet najis cloth?
A) Always, as long as the wet cloth is najis.
B) Only if the wet cloth can be squeezed and liquid drips.
C) Only if the wet cloth is najis by 'ayniyya impurity.
D) Never, because cloth does not transfer impurity.

Key Takeaway
Impurity transfers only when moisture can be squeezed or flows; mere dampness does not transmit najasa.

Impurity Transmission Through Moisture: The Drip Condition
Ruling on impurity transmission when wet najis cloth contacts dry pure cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition of 'dripping when pressed' to determine whether a pure object becomes impure through contact with a wet najis object.

Core Idea
Impurity only transfers through flowing liquid, not mere dampness.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq: whether a dry pure cloth becomes impure when placed in contact with a wet najis cloth. The key distinction is whether the moisture can be squeezed out (yan'aṣiru). We will explore the ruling, its rationale, and apply it to other everyday scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
State the scenario: a wet najis cloth is wrapped in a dry pure cloth. The ruling: the pure cloth does not become impure, provided that when pressed, no liquid drips.
Focus on the precise condition: 'if pressed, it does not drip'.
2
Understand the condition
The condition is that the moisture must be capable of being squeezed out (yan'aṣiru). If it only leaves dampness (nadāwah) without flowing, no impurity transfers.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between flowing liquid and mere dampness.
3
Identify the rationale
The reason is that impurity (najāsah) transfers only when a part of the najis substance separates and moves to the pure object. Dampness without flow does not carry particles.
This is based on the principle that impurity is transmitted by liquid that runs.
4
Apply to analogous cases
The commentary lists examples: wet cloth on a dry najis rope, washed foot on impure ground, sweating on a najis bed – if no trace appears, no impurity. But walking with a dry foot on wet impure ground does transfer impurity.
The key is whether moisture transfers from the impure to the pure object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لُفَّ ثوب نجس رطب في ثوب طاهر يابس، فظهر رطوبته على ثوب طاهر لكن لا ينعصر لو عصر، لا ينجس. لا ينجس إلخ أي لا يتنجس الثوب الطاهر؛ لأنه إذا لم يتقاطر من الثوب النجس بالعصر لا ينفصل منه شيء، وإنما يبتل ما يجاوره بالنداوة، وبذلك لا يتنجس، وعلى هذا إذا نشر الثوب المبلول على حبل نجس وهو يابس لا يتنجس الثوب، أو غسل رجله ومشى على أرض نجسة، أو نام على فراش فعرق ولم يظهر أثره ، لا ينجس، ولو مشى على أرض رطبة نجسة ورجله يابس تتنجس. (عيني، فتح)
A wet najis cloth is wrapped in a dry pure cloth, and its moisture appears on the pure cloth, but if pressed it does not drip, it does not become impure. 'Does not become impure etc.' means the pure cloth does not become impure because when nothing drips from the najis cloth by pressure, no part separates; rather, what is adjacent becomes moist by dampness, and that does not make it impure. Based on this, if one spreads a wet cloth on a dry najis rope, the cloth does not become impure; or if one washes his foot and walks on impure ground, or sleeps on a bed and sweats without its trace appearing, it does not become impure. But if one walks on wet impure ground with a dry foot, it becomes impure. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Kanz al-Daqaiq on the transmission of ritual impurity (najasah) through moisture. The matn states: if a wet najis cloth is wrapped in a dry pure cloth and moisture appears on the pure cloth but does not drip when pressed, the pure cloth does not become impure. The commentary from 'Ayni and Fath expands: the reason is that no moisture transfers; only dampness (nadaawah) contacts, which is insufficient for najasah transmission. The rule is applied to other cases: a wet cloth on a dry najis rope, walking with washed feet on impure ground, sweating on a bed without visible trace—all do not cause impurity. However, if one's dry foot walks on wet impure ground, it becomes impure because moisture transfers. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that impurity (najasah) only transmits through flowing or transferring liquid.

Key Terms
ينعصر (yan'aṣiru): To be squeezed out; here it means that liquid flows when pressed.
نداوة (nadāwah): Dampness or moisture that does not run; insufficient for impurity transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does a dry pure cloth become impure when a wet najis cloth is placed on it and moisture appears but does not drip when pressed?
A) Yes, it becomes impure
B) No, it does not become impure
C) It depends on the type of impurity
D) It becomes impure only if the cloth is also najis

Key Takeaway
Impurity transfers only through flowing liquid that can be squeezed out, not through mere dampness.

Purification by Fire: Istihalah in Action
Ruling on purification of a bloodied goat's head by burning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification by burning and apply the principle of istihalah to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Burning transforms impurity, making the substance pure — istihalah in action.

You may have encountered the rule that water purifies najasah. But what if water is unavailable or the impurity is on a food item? The Hanafi school recognizes that fire can also purify by consuming the impurity, a process called istihalah. This lesson examines a concrete case: a goat's head smeared with blood, burned until the blood disappears. Can you make soup from it? Let's see the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the matn
Identify the specific legal judgment: a goat's head smeared with blood, burned until blood disappears, then soup is made – it is permissible (jāz) and this is the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ).
The matn of Kanz al-Daqāʾiq is the source.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is the principle that burning is like washing (al-ḥarqu kā al-ghusl) and examples of istihālah: feces to ash, wine to vinegar, pig to salt.
These examples show transformation of the substance.
3
Understand the reasoning
Fire consumes the impurity, causing a transformation (istihālah), so the substance becomes pure. This is analogous to chemical changes where the original najis matter no longer exists.
The key is complete consumption, not mere removal.
4
Consider other schools
Some schools may not accept burning as purification for solids, but the Hanafi view is adopted as al-ṣaḥīḥ (the sound position).
Cross-madhhab ikhtilāf exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأس شاة متلطخ بالدم، أحرق وزال عنه الدم، فاتخذ منه مرقة جاز، وهو الصحيح والحرق كالغسل. كالغسل إلخ لأن النار تأكل ما فيه من النجاسة، ولهذا لو أحرقت العذرة، وصارت رمادا طهرت؛ للاستحالة، كالخمر إذا تخللت وكالخنزير إذا وقع في المملحة، وصار ملحا وعلى هذا قالوا: إذا تنجس التنور يطهر بالنار يتنجس الخبز، وكذا إذا تنجست ممسحة الخباز تطهر بالنار. (فتح)
A goat's head smeared with blood, burned and the blood disappears, then soup is made from it: it is permissible, and this is the correct view. And burning is like washing. 'Like washing etc.' because fire consumes the impurity, and therefore if one burns feces and it becomes ash, it becomes pure due to transformation (istihalah), like vinegar when it turns from wine, and like a pig if it falls into a salt mine and becomes salt. Based on this, they said: if an oven becomes impure, it is purified by fire, even if bread becomes impure (from the fire?), and similarly if a baker's wiping cloth becomes impure, it is purified by fire. (Fath)
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding the purification of a goat's head that was smeared with blood. The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states: if the head is burned until the blood is gone, it is permissible to make soup from it, and this is the correct view. The reasoning (provided in the commentary from Fath al-Qadir) is that burning is equivalent to washing because fire consumes the impurity. This is an application of the principle of istihalah (transformation): when a najis substance undergoes a complete transformation into a different substance, it becomes pure. Examples: feces burned to ash, wine turning to vinegar, a pig turning into salt. The commentary extends this to purifying an oven or a baker's wiping cloth by burning the impurity. The ruling is based on the idea that the impurity is eliminated, not merely removed.

Key Terms
استحالة (istiḥālah): Transformation of a substance into another, rendering it pure.
الحرق كالغسل (al-ḥarqu kā al-ghusl): Burning (with fire) is equivalent to washing (with water) in purifying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible to make soup from a goat's head that was burned to remove blood?
A) The fire kills the germs.
B) The fire consumes the impurity, transforming the head, similar to chemical changes.
C) The blood evaporates and the head becomes pure by evaporation.
D) The fire only removes the blood physically, leaving the head pure.

Key Takeaway
Burning can purify a najis substance by consuming the impurity through istihālah, a unique Hanafi principle.

The Legal Ruling of Male Circumcision
Ruling on circumcision with conditions and timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on male circumcision and identify the conditions that affect its validity and exemptions.

Core Idea
Circumcision is a sunnah muakkadah, not fard; its cutting is required only if the glans is covered, and exemptions exist for those who cannot bear it.

In this lesson, we examine the fiqh of circumcision (khitan) according to the Hanafi school. The text clarifies the legal status, the condition for cutting the prepuce, and special cases such as an elderly convert. Understanding these rulings is essential for distinguishing between sunnah and fard obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
The text states that circumcision is a 'sunnah of the symbols of Islam', marking it as sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school, not fard or wajib.
The status is crucial because it determines whether a person is sinful for abandoning it or merely missing a reward.
2
Determine the condition for cutting the prepuce
If the glans (hashafah) is already visible, there is no need to cut. The skin should only be removed if it covers the glans.
This condition is based on the purpose of circumcision: to expose the glans.
3
Recognise the exemption for the elderly convert
An old man who converts to Islam and cannot bear the procedure is not required to undergo circumcision; it is left as is.
The exemption applies due to incapacity.
4
Understand the ruling on partial circumcision
If more than half of the foreskin is cut, it counts as valid circumcision; half or less does not.
This follows the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole.
5
Note the imam's duty if circumcision is abandoned
If an entire town agrees to abandon circumcision, the imam should fight them because it is a symbol of Islam.
This shows the communal importance despite it not being obligatory individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حشفته ظاهرة بحيث لو رأى إنسان ظنه مختونا، ولا يقطع جلد ذكره إلا بتشديد، والحال أنه لا يقطع ترك كشيخ أسلم، وقال أهل البصر : لا يطيق الختان، ووقته سبع سنين. والمسابقة أي كما يترك أي أهل العلم من الحجامين بالفرس والإبل والأرجل والرمي أي ابتداء وقت الختان استخلاصه - ويقرض القاضي مال اليتيم ويكتب الصك بخلاف الأب والوصي والملتقط؛ لأنهم عاجزون عن فيكون تضييعا إلا أن الملتقط إذا أنشد اللقطة ومضى مدة النشد ينبغي أن يجوز له الإقراض من الفقراء؛ لأنه لو تصدق به عليهم في هذه الحالة جاز فالقرض أولى. ترك إلخ : أي ترك قطع الجلد؛ لأن قطع جلد ذكره لتنكشف الحشفة، فإذا كانت الحشفة ظاهرة؛ فلا حاجة إلى القطع، وإن كان يواري الحشفة يقطع الفضل، ولو ختن ولم تقطع الجلدة كلها ينظر إن قطع أكثر من النصف يكون ختانا؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وإن قطع النصف فما دونه لا يعتد به لعدم الختان حقيقة وحكما. [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٠/٢] كشيخ أسلم إلخ : أي كما يترك قطع جلد الشيخ الذي أسلم، وهو الختان؛ لأن عذره ظاهر، قال في "الفتح" اعلم أن الختان سنة من شعائر الإسلام، وخصائصه فلو اجتمع أهل بلدة على تركه حاربهم الإمام كذا في "التنوير" وختان المرأة ليس بسنة بل مكرمة للرجال؛ لأنه ألذ في الجماع وقيل سنة: قال في الدر المختار" وقد جمع السيوطي من ولد مختونا من الأنبياء الله فقال: وفي الرسل مختون لعمرك خلقة ثمان وتسع وهم زكريا شيث إدريس يوسف وحنظلة ونوح شعیب سام طيبون أكارم وموسى وآدم عیسی لوط و صالح سليمان يحيى هود يسن خاتم لا يطيق ووقته إلخ قال ملا مسكين أي ابتداء وقته سبع سنين، وذكر في "الذخيرة" أقصى وقته اثنتي عشرة سنة. قال في "التكملة" أي وقت الختان سبع سنين، وقيل: لا يختن حتى يبلغ؛ لأن الختان للطهارة، ولا طهارة عليه قبله، فكان إيلاما قبله من غير حاجة، وقيل: أقصاه اثنا عشر سنة، وقيل: تسع سنين، وقيل: وقته عشر سنين؛ لأنه يؤمر بالصلاة إذا بلغ عشرا اعتيادا أو تخلقا، فيحتاج إلى الختان؛ لأنه شرع للطهارة، وقيل: إن كان قويا يطيق ألم الختان يختن وإلا فلا، وهو أشبه بالفقه، وقال أبو حنيفة : لا علم لي بوقته ولم يرد عن أبي يوسف ومحمد فيه شيء، وإن المشايخ اختلفوا فيه.
His foreskin is apparent such that if a person saw him, he would think he is circumcised, so the skin of his penis is not cut except with difficulty, and the situation is that he does not cut it, it is left like a sheikh who became Muslim. And the people of Basra said: he cannot bear circumcision, and its time is seven years. And the competition, meaning as it is left, meaning the scholars among the cupper, with horse, camel, foot, and archery, meaning the beginning of the time of circumcision, its extraction. And the judge lends the orphan's property and writes a deed, contrary to the father, executor, and finder, because they are incapable of [suing?] so it would be waste. Except that the finder, if he announces the lost property and the period of announcement passes, it is permissible for him to lend to the poor, because if he gives charity to them in this situation, it is permissible, so lending is more appropriate. 'He left' etc.: meaning he leaves cutting the skin, because cutting the skin of his penis is to uncover the glans; if the glans is apparent, there is no need to cut, and if it covers the glans, he cuts the excess. And if he is circumcised and not all the skin is cut, it is considered: if he cut more than half, it is circumcision, because the majority has the ruling of the whole; if he cuts half or less, it is not counted, because there is no circumcision in reality and law. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/510] 'Like a sheikh who became Muslim' etc.: meaning just as the skin of a sheikh who became Muslim is left uncut, which is circumcision, because his excuse is apparent. He said in al-Fath: Know that circumcision is a sunnah of the symbols of Islam and its special characteristics; if the people of a town agree to abandon it, the imam should fight them, as in al-Tanwir. And female circumcision is not sunnah but a honor for men because it is more pleasurable in intercourse, and it is said it is sunnah. He said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: al-Suyuti collected those prophets who were born circumcised, and said: Among the messengers, there are eight or nine born circumcised, and they are: Zakariyya, Sheeth, Idris, Yusuf, Hanzala, Nuh, Shuayb, Sam, Tayyibun, Akarim, Musa, Adam, Isa, Lut, Salih, Sulayman, Yahya, Hud, Yasin, Khatam. 'He cannot bear' and 'its time' etc. Mulla Miskin said: the beginning of its time is seven years, and it is mentioned in al-Dhakhira: the latest time is twelve years. He said in al-Takmila: the time of circumcision is seven years, and it is said: do not circumcise until he reaches puberty, because circumcision is for purity, and there is no purity upon him before that, so it would be causing pain without need. And it is said: its maximum is twelve, and it is said: nine years, and it is said: its time is ten years, because he is commanded to pray when he reaches ten as a habit or as a trait, so he needs circumcision because it is legislated for purity. And it is said: if he is strong and can bear the pain of circumcision, he is circumcised; otherwise not, and that is more in accordance with fiqh. And Abu Hanifa said: I have no knowledge of its time, and nothing has been reported from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad about it, and the shaykhs differed on it.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on circumcision (khitan) covering several aspects. First, it states that if the glans is already visible, there is no need to cut the prepuce. The case of an old man who converts to Islam is exempted if he cannot bear the procedure. The ruling on partial circumcision: cutting more than half is valid, half or less is not. The timing is discussed extensively: the recommended age is seven, with maximum up to twelve in some views. The passage also notes that female circumcision is not sunnah but a commendable act (mukrama). Finally, Abu Hanifa said there is no specific fixed time, and the scholars differed.

Key Terms
الختان (al-khitan): The act of circumcision, cutting the prepuce of the penis.
الحشفة (al-hashafah): The glans of the penis.
مكرمة (mukramah): A commendable act, not a sunnah, specifically for female circumcision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of male circumcision?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mubah
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Male circumcision is sunnah muakkadah, performed when the foreskin covers the glans, with exemptions for those who cannot bear it.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Timing of Circumcision and Female Circumcision in the Hanafi School
Ruling on circumcision with conditions and timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi opinions on the recommended age for male circumcision and explain the status of female circumcision.

Core Idea
Circumcision is recommended at age seven, with maximum at twelve; female circumcision is not sunnah but a commendable act (mukrama).

This lesson explores the diverse opinions within the Hanafi school regarding the timing of male circumcision and the ruling on female circumcision. Abu Hanifa himself stated no fixed time, while later scholars recommended seven years. Additionally, the text clarifies that female circumcision is not sunnah but an honorable practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended starting time
Mulla Miskin states that the beginning of the time is seven years. This is the most widely cited opinion.
Seven years is the age when a child can typically endure the procedure.
2
Note the maximum time according to al-Dhakhira
The latest time is twelve years, as mentioned in al-Dhakhira.
Other opinions mention nine or ten years, but twelve is the maximum.
3
Recognise Abu Hanifa's position and the silence of the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa said: 'I have no knowledge of its time.' Nothing is reported from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. This indicates flexibility.
The lack of a fixed time suggests it is not an urgent obligation.
4
Understand the rationale behind the timing
Circumcision is for purification; prayer becomes obligatory at ten, so it should be done before that to accustom the child. Also, some say it should wait until puberty because there is no purity before that.
The opinion that it should be done when the child can bear pain is 'more in accordance with fiqh'.
5
Discuss female circumcision
The text from al-Fath says female circumcision is not sunnah but a 'mukrama' (honorable act) for men because it makes intercourse more pleasurable. Some say it is sunnah, but the Hanafi position is that it is not sunnah.
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i school which considers it sunnah.

According to the Hanafi school, what is the latest recommended age for male circumcision?
